### Wikipedia Scraper Final Results (Completed 5:12 AM)

**Status:** ✅ SUCCESS - Zero errors
**Runtime:** 8 hours 20 minutes (8:51 PM Mar 4 → 5:12 AM Mar 5)
**Completion:** 1 hour ahead of schedule (ETA was 6:15 AM)

**Coverage achieved:**
- Players processed: 3,611/3,652 (98.9%)

- With meaningful college stats: 983 (28.5% of found)

- Errors: 0
- Database: 3,451 records inserted to historical_stats.db

**Performance vs projections (from 10:26 PM Mar 4 check):**
- Find rate: 95.6% actual vs 99.2% projected (-3.6%, still excellent)
- Stats rate: 28.5% actual vs 52.8% projected (-24.3%, significant variance)
- Players with stats: 983 actual vs ~1,913 projected (-930 players)
- Completion time: 5:12 AM actual vs 6:15 AM projected (1 hour early)

**Why stats rate was lower than projected:**
- Early sample (620 players at 10:26 PM) biased toward players WITH stats tables
- 52.8% stats rate was based on first 17% of dataset (select sample)
- Later players (backups, special teamers, UDFA) had Wikipedia pages but no college stats tables
- Long tail of NFL players explains 28.5% final rate vs 52.8% early estimate

**Data quality metrics:**
- Average confidence: 0.33 (on 0-1 scale)
- Average search score: 0.763 (Wikipedia page match quality)
- Unique players: 2,970 (some players have multiple draft years/records)
- Total records: 3,451
- Database: historical_stats.db (wikipedia_college_stats table)

## Dual Expert Validation Complete - Critical Findings (7:12-7:22 AM EST)

### Taylor's Decision (7:12 AM)

**Agent 2:** validate-wikipedia-data-quality (researcher, Opus, 30-min timeout)

### Data Quality Validation Results (Completed 7:18 AM, 4m12s runtime)

**Agent:** validate-wikipedia-data-quality
**Grade:** D+
**Status:** ⚠️ CRITICAL ISSUES FOUND

**Critical findings:**

1. **🔴 NFL Contamination (286 records, 29% of "meaningful stats")**
   - Scraper grabbed wrong table from Wikipedia (NFL career stats, not college)
   - Examples: Ryan Fitzpatrick 34,990 "college" pass yards (actually NFL career), Emmitt Smith 18,355 "college" rush yards (actually NFL career)
   - Would poison ML model if used as-is

2. **🔴 ALL 19 Famous Players Missing**
   - Tom Brady, Peyton Manning, Aaron Rodgers, Saquon Barkley, Calvin Johnson, Travis Kelce, Rob Gronkowski, etc.
   - Scraper's player lookup failing on most important entries

3. **Only ~688 truly clean records**
   - After filtering college_games > 60 (NFL contamination indicator)
   - 980 "meaningful stats" → 688 verified clean (30% loss)

4. **Data quality issues:**
   - 481 NULL draft_years (13.9%)
   - 103 "NaN" college names
   - 40+ position name variants (needs normalization)
   - 118 wrong Wikipedia URLs

5. **✅ When data IS present and clean, accuracy is high**
   - Mahomes, Moss, Peterson, Gonzalez verified correct against Wikipedia
   - Core extraction logic works when it finds right table

**Recommendations:**
- Filter records with college_games > 60 to remove NFL contamination
- Fix scraper's player lookup to capture missing stars
- Normalize positions, fix NaN values
- Target 1,500+ verified records before production ML

**Report:** `~/.openclaw/workspace-titlerun/research/wikipedia-data-quality-report.md`

## Wikipedia Scraper Fix Agent Deployed (7:22-7:37 AM EST)

### Taylor's Decision (7:22 AM)

**Command:** "Let's fix the issues from Wikipedia"

**Context:** Dual expert validation found critical bugs in Wikipedia data (D+ grade, 30% NFL contamination, all famous players missing)

### Fix Agent Deployed (7:22 AM)

**Agent:** fix-wikipedia-scraper (researcher, Opus, high thinking, 45-min timeout)
**ETA:** ~8:07 AM
**Mission:** Fix table detection + player lookup bugs, clean data, achieve 98%+ coverage with 0% contamination

**Critical bugs to fix:**

1. **Bug 1: Table Detection (30% NFL Contamination)**
   - Problem: Scraper grabbing first table on Wikipedia = often NFL career stats
   - Evidence: Ryan Fitzpatrick 34,990 "college" pass yards (actually NFL), Emmitt Smith 18,355 "college" rush yards (actually NFL)
   - 286/980 records contaminated (29%)
   - Fix strategy: Target tables with "College"/"NCAA" in caption, validate column headers, check games-per-row (1-15 college vs 16-17 NFL)

2. **Bug 2: Player Lookup (All Famous Players Missing)**
   - Problem: All 19 famous players missing (Brady, Manning, Rodgers, Saquon, Kelce, Gronk, Calvin Johnson, etc.)
   - Hypothesis: Search too strict, name variations not handled, fuzzy match threshold too high
   - Fix strategy: Add fallback strategies (try exact name, remove Jr./Sr./III, try first+last only), lower fuzzy threshold

3. **Bug 3: Data Quality Issues**
   - 481 NULL draft_years (13.9%)
   - 103 "NaN" college names
   - 40+ position name variants needing normalization
   - Fix: Add post-extraction validation, filter extreme values, clean existing DB

**Code changes required:**
- `wikipedia_scraper.py`: Add find_college_stats_table() function with header validation
- `wikipedia_search.py`: Add search_player_with_fallbacks() function with name variation handling
- Database cleanup: DELETE contaminated records, fix NaN values, normalize positions
- Re-run on famous players to validate fixes

**Deliverables expected:**
1. Fixed code (wikipedia_scraper.py, wikipedia_search.py)
2. Test results CSV (before/after validation)
3. Clean database (286 contaminated records removed)
4. Re-run results on 19 famous players (should all be found)
5. Summary report: FIX_REPORT.md

**Success criteria:**
| Metric | Before | Target After |
|--------|--------|--------------|
| Clean records | 688 | 1,500+ |
| NFL contamination | 286 (29%) | 0 (0%) |
| Famous players found | 0/19 | 19/19 ✅ |
| Coverage | 72% | 98%+ |
| Data quality grade | D+ | B+ |

**Timeline:** 45 minutes, ETA ~8:07 AM

**Status (7:37 AM):** Agent running, 15 minutes elapsed, ~30 minutes remaining

## Phase 1 Architecture Review Read (7:40-7:43 AM EST)

### Taylor's Request (7:40 AM)

**Command:** "Let's read the review together from last night"

**Context:** Phase 1 architecture review completed 10:42 PM Mar 4 but output never delivered to main session, needed to locate and read

### Architecture Review Located (7:40 AM)

**File found:** `/Users/jeffdaniels/.openclaw/workspace-researcher/research/phase1-architecture-review.md`
**Reviewer:** Fury (Senior ML Architecture Review agent)
**Date:** 2026-03-04
**Document reviewed:** phase1-ml-architecture.md (58KB, 1,370 lines)
**Context:** Architecture designed in ~8 minutes, reviewed before 4-week implementation commitment

### Overall Assessment

**Grade:** B+ / Strong Foundation with Critical Gaps
**Verdict:** PROCEED with implementation after fixing 5 must-fix items (2-3 hours work)

**What's good:**
- Conformal prediction via CQR is correct methodology
- Full-population training on 5,434 players (eliminates survivor bias)
- Walk-forward expanding window validation correct
- DB-bridge integration pattern smart
- Time-decay weighting well-reasoned
- 1A → 1B migration path (single model first, position-specific if validated) correct sequencing

**What's concerning:**
- MAPIE API usage appears incorrect (code may not compile)
- Calibration set dangerously small (single season ~1,500-2,000 player-seasons)
- No explicit exchangeability discussion (conformal guarantees require it)
- Missing scoring system handling (PPR only, no path to half-PPR/standard)
- Timeline aggressive (4 weeks tight even with clean data)
- Data readiness assumed not verified
- Classification outputs mathematically wrong (ad-hoc interpolation, not real probabilities)

### MUST-FIX Items (Block Implementation)

1. **Verify MAPIE API usage** - Code sample likely doesn't work, test before committing, have manual CQR backup (1 hour)
2. **Fix classification outputs** - Remove fake breakout/bust probabilities OR train separate classifier (30 min)
3. **Add scoring system strategy** - Decide PPR-only vs multi-format before building (2 hours design)
4. **Rebalance Week 1** - Move MAPIE integration to Week 2, Week 1: data verification + features + dataset + baselines + initial LightGBM (0 hours, timeline edit)
5. **Add fallback logic** - Ceiling clip (35 PPG max), exception handling, persistence-baseline fallback (1 hour)

### SHOULD-FIX Items (Address Week 1-2)

6. Increase calibration set size (use 2+ seasons)
7. Add baseline model ladder (linear regression, elastic net between baselines and LightGBM)
8. Add college dominator rating + WOPR to Tier 1 features (proven predictors, 96%+ coverage)
9. Handle zero-inflated target distribution (30-40% players score 0 PPG, consider two-stage model)
10. Add era normalization (league-wide PPG normalization as feature)
11. Define position-specific pass/fail criteria (not just overall MAE)
12. Use LightGBM native serialization (not pickle - security + portability)
13. Add Day 0 data verification (before Week 1 starts)

### Alternative Approaches Identified

**Alt 1: Skip conformal prediction in Phase 1, add in Phase 1.1**
- Simpler, faster implementation
- But loses uncertainty quantification (priority #2 from expert audits)
- Recommendation: Keep conformal but move to Week 2 (after base model working)

**Alt 2: Two-stage model (zero-inflated)**
- Stage 1: Binary classifier (will they play? P(PPG > 2))
- Stage 2: Regression conditional on playing
- Handles massive zero-inflation naturally, gives "bust probability" for free
- Recommendation: Strong candidate for Week 2 if single-stage struggles

**Alt 3: Ensemble (LightGBM + linear model)**
- Simple average or stacked blend of tree + elastic net
- Linear regularizes tree's overfitting
- Recommendation: Worth trying Week 2, low effort, potentially meaningful improvement

### Timeline Assessment

**Original estimate:** 4 weeks (28 days, 7 days/week, no buffer)
**Revised realistic:** 5-6 weeks with buffer

**Adjusted timeline:**
- Week 1: Data verification + feature engineering + dataset + baselines + initial LightGBM (removed MAPIE)
- Week 2: Conformal prediction (MAPIE or manual CQR) + hyperparameter tuning + calibration validation
- Week 3: Position analysis (1A vs 1B) + classification outputs (separate model) + feature selection (NEW)
- Week 4: Production integration (DB schema + batch pipeline + Node.js bridge) + testing
- Week 5: A/B comparison + UAT with Taylor + refinement + monitoring
- Buffer: 3-5 days for unexpected issues

**Why 5-6 weeks:**
- Data cleaning always takes 50% longer
- MAPIE integration + calibration validation = standalone week
- 1A vs 1B decision requires running both, comparing, documenting
- Integration testing will surface bugs requiring Python-side fixes
- UAT should be in-timeline, not post-deployment

**Compressed option (keep 4 weeks):**
- Skip Optuna tuning (use defaults: lr=0.05, n_estimators=500, max_depth=6)
- Skip LODCO validation
- Skip position-specific models (1A only)
- Skip classification outputs (defer to Phase 1.1)
- Skip monitoring dashboard (logging only)
- Still delivers: Full-population LightGBM + CQR intervals + walk-forward validation + DB bridge integration

### Key Decisions Needed from Taylor

1. **Scoring systems:** PPR-only for Phase 1, or build multi-format now?
2. **Timeline:** Compress to 4 weeks (cut scope) or realistic 5-6 weeks?
3. **Conformal prediction:** Keep in Phase 1 (Week 2) or defer to Phase 1.1?

### Risk Assessment

**Biggest risk:** Timeline pressure causing corners to be cut on validation (model without proper calibration = false certainty, worse than no model)

**Other risks identified:**
- Persistence baseline harder to beat than expected (ML often only 5-10% better, not 15-20%)
- MAPIE has breaking changes or bugs (young library, v0.8.x)
- Full-population data reveals most features don't matter (signal-to-noise ratio plummets)
- Node.js ↔ Python integration clunkier than expected (schema mismatches, encoding issues, NULL handling)
- Users don't understand or trust prediction intervals (want single number, not range)

### Final Verdict

**Implementation readiness:** Mostly ready with caveats

**Ready:**
- Technology choices sound (LightGBM + MAPIE + PostgreSQL)
- Feature set well-defined (Tier 1 clear and comprehensive)
- Validation strategy correct (walk-forward expanding window)
- Integration pattern simple and appropriate (DB bridge)
- File structure and module decomposition clean

**Not ready:**
- MAPIE API usage needs verification
- Scoring system decision not made
- Classification output design flawed
- Data readiness not confirmed (Wikipedia scrape still running at review time)
- Week 1 scope too large

**Recommendation:** Proceed after 5 MUST-FIX items addressed (2-3 hours total design-level fixes, not multi-day efforts). Architecture fundamentally sound.

**Grade:** B+ → A- with must-fixes addressed

_Phase 1 architecture review read: 2026-03-05 7:40-7:43 AM EST - comprehensive 11,000-word expert review by Fury, grade B+ (strong foundation with critical gaps), 5 must-fix items (MAPIE API, classification outputs, scoring system, Week 1 rebalance, fallback logic), 12 should-fix items, 3 alternative approaches, timeline adjustment 4 weeks → 5-6 weeks realistic (or compress with scope cuts), key decisions needed: PPR-only vs multi-format, 4 vs 5-6 week timeline, conformal in Phase 1 or 1.1, final verdict: proceed after must-fixes (2-3 hours), architecture fundamentally sound_

## Phase 1 Architecture Fix Teams Complete (7:47-8:00 AM EST)

### Taylor's Decision (7:47 AM)

**Command:** "Let's deploy all teams in parallel"

**Context:** Phase 1 architecture review identified 5 MUST-FIX + 12 SHOULD-FIX items, proposed 3 parallel expert teams to address all fixes

### All 3 Teams Deployed (7:47 AM)

**Team 1:** fix-mapie-technical (researcher, Opus, 60-min timeout)
**Team 2:** fix-model-architecture (researcher, Opus, 60-min timeout)
**Team 3:** fix-implementation-planning (researcher, Opus, 60-min timeout)

**Parallel execution:** All 3 teams + Wikipedia fix agent running simultaneously

### Team 2: Model Architecture Complete (7:56 AM, 6m40s runtime)

**Agent:** fix-model-architecture
**Deliverable:** `phase1-model-fixes.md` (1,209 lines)
**Status:** ✅ ALL 7 DECISIONS MADE

**Decisions:**

1. **Classification outputs:** Dense quantile regression (19 quantile levels) to approximate CDF
   - Mathematically sound replacement for fake interpolation
   - Reuses same LightGBM framework
   - Probabilities learned, not hardcoded

2. **Scoring systems:** PPR primary, derive Standard/Half-PPR via receptions adjustment
   - One model, exact linear transformation
   - PPR is 70%+ of dynasty leagues

3. **Enhanced Tier 1 features:** Added college dominator rating, WOPR, target share, snap%, receptions_per_game
   - 27 features total (was 22)
   - Dominator rating = #1 cited WR predictor
   - NaN masking for position-irrelevant features

4. **Baseline ladder:** 5 models (Intercept → Linear → Elastic Net → Random Forest → LightGBM)
   - Decision rule: if LightGBM < 5% better than Elastic Net, ship Elastic Net instead

5. **Zero-inflated distribution:** Two-stage model (relevance gate + conditional PPG regression)
   - Stage 1: Binary classifier P(PPG > 2.0)
   - Stage 2: Quantile regression on relevant players only
   - Bust probability comes free

6. **Era normalization:** Add ppg_vs_league_avg, ppg_z_score, ppg_percentile_rank features
   - Complements time-decay weighting (not redundant)
   - Time-decay = training strategy, era features = predictive signal

7. **Success criteria:** 7 precise metrics with Must-Pass/Target/Stretch thresholds
   - Persistence baseline defined for returning players and rookies
   - COVID fold excluded from pass/fail
   - Position-specific thresholds

**Implementation impact:** 14 hours estimated, no architectural redesign, all fixes work within existing framework

### Team 1: MAPIE + Technical Complete (7:57 AM, 8m54s runtime)

**Agent:** fix-mapie-technical
**Deliverable:** `phase1-technical-fixes.md` (54KB)
**Status:** ✅ ALL 6 FIXES COMPLETE WITH TESTED CODE

**Critical discovery:** Architecture doc's MAPIE code was completely broken
- `MapieQuantileRegressor` doesn't exist in MAPIE 1.x (renamed to `ConformalizedQuantileRegressor`)
- API completely changed: `.fit(X, y, X_calib=...)` became `.fit(X, y).conformalize(X_cal, y_cal)`
- `alpha` parameter must be set on LGBMRegressor constructor

**Fixes delivered:**

1. **MAPIE API usage:** Corrected to `ConformalizedQuantileRegressor` with `.fit().conformalize()` pipeline (TESTED)

2. **Manual CQR backup:** 80-line standalone implementation, 0.940 coverage (equivalent to MAPIE's 0.933) (TESTED)

3. **Fallback logic:** NaN handling, 35 PPG ceiling, inverted interval fix, persistence baseline fallback (DESIGNED)

4. **Serialization:** LightGBM native `.save_model()` + numpy + JSON, round-trip verified identical predictions (TESTED)

5. **Calibration:** 2022-2023 two-season calibration (doubles n_cal to ~1,000-1,200), exchangeability preserved (DESIGNED)

6. **Integration test:** 6 test functions, all passing on MAPIE 1.3.0 + LightGBM 4.6.0 (ALL PASS)

**Key recommendation:** Use ManualCQR as primary implementation (not MAPIE). MAPIE broke backward compatibility between 0.8.x and 1.x. ManualCQR produces equivalent results with zero dependency risk.

### Team 3: Implementation Planning Complete (7:59 AM, 7m54s runtime)

**Agent:** fix-implementation-planning
**Deliverable:** `phase1-implementation-plan.md` (82KB)
**Status:** ✅ ALL 7 FIXES INCORPORATED

**Fixes delivered:**

1. **Week 1 rebalanced:** Split 7 deliverables into 7 days with clear daily tasks, LightGBM/MAPIE/validation moved to Week 2

2. **Revised 6-week roadmap:** Complete day-by-day breakdown with visual timeline, dependency map, exit gates at each week boundary

3. **Day 0 data verification:** 10-item checklist with pass/fail criteria, complete Python validation script (`day0_validation.py`), go/no-go decision matrix, CFBD-only fallback plan

4. **Precise success criteria:** 3 primary (must-pass) + 4 secondary criteria with exact thresholds, complete `evaluate_success_criteria()` Python function, reporting template

5. **Integration testing plan:** Full schema definition with CHECK constraints, 3-layer testing (Python → DB, DB → Node.js, end-to-end), 8+ pytest cases, 4+ Jest cases, common pitfalls table

6. **Compressed 4-week option:** Complete timeline with explicit scope cuts (Optuna, LODCO, position models, classification, monitoring dashboard), risk assessment, Phase 1.1 backlog with effort estimates (~2 weeks)

7. **Retraining cadence:** Annual lifecycle diagram, 4 retraining triggers, complete `DriftMonitor` class, model versioning scheme (v1.0 → v1.1 → v2.0), post-season monitoring SQL

**Additional highlights:**
- 12 risks identified with probability, impact, owner, mitigation
- 6 go/no-go gates with escalation procedures

## Critical Analysis of Phase 1 Reconciliation Decisions (8:44-8:47 AM EST)

### Taylor's Challenge (8:44 AM)

**Quote:** "Can you walk me through the changes to the Phase 1 reconciliation? I want to ensure this is actually the best path forward for the modeling and success of the business vs. you being lazy."

**Context:** Taylor concerned that simplified decisions might be shortcuts rather than smart tradeoffs

### Honest Assessment of 4 Key Decisions

**Decision 1: 3 Quantile Models (not 19) - ✅ SOUND, NOT LAZY**
- Quantile crossing affects 5-15% of predictions with 19 models (division-by-zero, negative probabilities)
- Serialization only designed for 3 models (would need complete redesign for 19)
- Testing showed ZERO crossings with 3 models
- Trade-off: Lose rich CDF for classification (P(breakout), P(bust) become coarse approximations)
- **Verdict:** Right call. Ship working predictions first, add rich classification later.
- **Alternative:** 7 quantiles with isotonic regression (adds ~1 day, better CDF approximation)

**Decision 2: PPR-Only (not multi-format) - ⚠️ SOUND BUT COSTLY, AGENT PARTIALLY LAZY**
- Math is ironclad: Converting PPR→Standard via estimated receptions breaks conformal coverage (90% becomes 75-80%)
- Shipping dishonest confidence intervals kills trust
- **BUT:** Loses 30% of market (Standard/Half-PPR leagues)
- **Agent's error:** Dismissed Option C (3 separate models) too quickly
  - Training time: 3 × 15 sec = 45 sec (trivial)
  - Storage: 9 files (trivial)
  - Real cost: 3× calibration + testing (adds 1.5 days, not 3 days)
- **Verdict:** Push back. Train 3 models with separate calibration. 30% market loss hurts more than 1.5 days work.
- **Recommendation:** Multi-format with proper per-format calibration (+1.5 days)

**Decision 3: Single-Stage (not two-stage) - 🔴 PARTIALLY LAZY**
- Agent's reasoning: Two-stage has Heckman selection bias + missing from timeline
- Trade-off: Lose explicit bust/breakout/starter probabilities (valuable product features)
- Agent's workaround: "q_10 = 0 IS bust signal" is a hack, not solution
- **Critical insight:** Agent's own Bug Fix #5 SOLVES selection bias with sample weighting!
- **Verdict:** YES, agent being lazy. Choosing "simple" over "correct" when fix already exists.
- **Recommendation:** Two-stage WITH sample weighting. Users want probabilities, not quantile approximations. Add ~2 days.

**Decision 4: ManualCQR (not MAPIE) - ✅ SOUND, SMART ENGINEERING**
- 80 lines of controlled numpy code vs library that already broke backward compatibility (0.8→1.0)
- Full visibility for production debugging
- Zero dependency risk
- **Verdict:** Absolutely correct. Not lazy - this is smart engineering.

**My assessment:** ⚠️ AGGRESSIVE BUT POSSIBLE IF scope accepted

**Risks:**
- Feature engineering: 2 days planned, 4 days realistic (audit)
- Player ID mapping: 2 days planned, 3-5 days realistic (audit)
- Integration always takes longer than planned

- Distributed buffer (2 days/week)
- Clear exit gates
- Decision point Day 12 (stop if model doesn't beat baseline)

**Recommended timeline with pushbacks:**
- Add back multi-format: +1.5 days
- Add back two-stage with sample weighting: +2 days
- **Total: 6.5-7 weeks realistic (28-30 active days with buffer)**
- Still better than 8-9 weeks, ships more complete product

## Multi-Format Architecture Discussion (8:47-8:50 AM EST)

### Taylor's Question (8:47 AM)

**Quote:** "Ok, how do we account for standard, half ppr and tep in the future?"

**Context:** After critical analysis of reconciliation decisions, need clarity on multi-format implementation strategy

### Three Architecture Options Presented

**Option 1: Separate Models Per Format (Recommended for Phase 1)**
- Train 4 separate LightGBM models (PPR, Standard, Half-PPR, TEP)
- Each model: own training data + conformal calibration + Q value
- Pros: Simple, guaranteed proper coverage (90% intervals cover 90%), easy debug
- Cons: 4× storage (12 model files), 4× training time (~60 sec total, trivial)
- Cost: +1.5 days to implement/test
- **Verdict:** Best for Phase 1 - simple, correct, fast to ship

**Option 2: PPR Model + Per-Format Recalibration (Phase 1.1)**
- Train ONE model on PPR, convert via reception adjustment
- Critical: Recalibrate conformal Q per format using format-specific residuals (Bug Fix #4)
- Pros: Only 3 LightGBM files, proper coverage if done correctly
- Cons: Requires reception estimation, more complex, estimation error creates noise
- **Verdict:** Optimize to this in Phase 1.1 after validating Option 1 works

**Option 3: Component-Based Prediction (Phase 2+)**
- Predict components (rush yards, rec yards, receptions, TDs) separately
- Scoring becomes pure math calculation
- Pros: Infinitely flexible (any scoring format), interpretable, no retraining for new rules
- Cons: 6 models (18 LightGBM files), complex error propagation, multivariate CQR
- **Verdict:** Long-term (6+ months) when maximum flexibility needed

### Recommendation for TitleRun

**Phase 1 (next 6-7 weeks):**
- Option 1: Train 4 separate models (PPR, Standard, Half-PPR, TEP)
- Each with proper conformal calibration
- Database schema: `scoring_format` column (enum)
- API: `GET /predictions?player_id=123&format=tep`
- Cost: +1.5 days
- Benefit: 100% market coverage with guaranteed correct intervals

**Phase 1.1 (~2-3 months):**
- Optimize to Option 2 (single PPR model + per-format recalibration)
- A/B test coverage on test set
- Switch if coverage ≥ 88% for all formats
- Reduces storage, maintains coverage

**Phase 2 (6+ months):**
- Option 3: Component-based predictions
- Support any scoring format including custom leagues
- Maximum interpretability

### Database Schema for Multi-Format

```sql
CREATE TABLE player_predictions (
    player_id INT,
    scoring_format VARCHAR(20),  -- 'ppr', 'standard', 'half_ppr', 'tep'
    season INT,
    ppg_floor DECIMAL(5,2),
    ppg_median DECIMAL(5,2),
    ppg_ceiling DECIMAL(5,2),
    confidence_level DECIMAL(3,2),  -- e.g., 0.90
    model_version VARCHAR(20),
    predicted_at TIMESTAMP,
    PRIMARY KEY (player_id, scoring_format, season),
    CHECK (scoring_format IN ('ppr', 'standard', 'half_ppr', 'tep')),
    CHECK (ppg_floor <= ppg_median),
    CHECK (ppg_median <= ppg_ceiling)
);
```

### Implementation Details (Option 1 for Phase 1)

```python
SCORING_FORMATS = {
    'ppr': {'rec_points': 1.0, 'te_bonus': 0.0},
    'standard': {'rec_points': 0.0, 'te_bonus': 0.0},
    'half_ppr': {'rec_points': 0.5, 'te_bonus': 0.0},
    'tep': {'rec_points': 1.0, 'te_bonus': 0.5}
}

for format_name, scoring in SCORING_FORMATS.items():
    y_train = calculate_ppg_for_format(
        historical_data, 
        scoring['rec_points'],
        scoring['te_bonus']
    )
    models[format_name] = train_cqr_models(X_train, y_train)
    Q[format_name] = calibrate_cqr(models[format_name], X_cal, y_cal)
```

### Key Decision Impact

**Original agent recommendation:** PPR-only (70% market)
**With Option 1 addition:** 4 formats (100% market coverage)
- Additional cost: +1.5 days
- Additional benefit: 30% more addressable market (Standard/Half-PPR leagues)
- Training time: 60 seconds total (trivial)
- Storage: 12 model files (trivial)

**Updated Phase 1 timeline with multi-format:**
- Original: 5 weeks active (6 with buffer)
- With multi-format: 5.5 weeks active (6.5-7 with buffer)
- Still beats 8-9 week original estimate

### Bottom Line

**Phase 1 approach:** Train 4 separate models (Option 1)
- Simple, correct, fast to implement
- Guaranteed proper conformal coverage for all formats
- 100% market coverage vs 70% with PPR-only
- Cost: +1.5 days (worth it for 30% more market)

**Future optimization path clear:**
- Phase 1.1: Consolidate to PPR + recalibration (Option 2)
- Phase 2+: Component-based for maximum flexibility (Option 3)

_Multi-format architecture defined: 2026-03-05 8:47-8:50 AM EST - 3 options presented (separate models, PPR+recalibration, component-based), recommended Option 1 for Phase 1 (4 separate models for PPR/Standard/Half-PPR/TEP, +1.5 days, 100% market coverage), future path Phase 1.1 optimize to single model, Phase 2+ component-based, database schema provided with scoring_format enum, training time 60 sec total trivial, addresses 30% market loss from PPR-only approach_

**Timeline breakdown:**

- Week 3: Add 0.5 days for multi-format DB schema
- Week 4: Add 1 day for multi-format UAT (20 players × 4 formats = 80 predictions)
- Week 5-6: Buffer + ship

### Model Architecture (Revised)

**Total models to train:**
- 4 scoring formats (PPR, Standard, Half-PPR, TEP)
- 2 stages per format (1 binary classifier + 3 quantile regressors)
- 4 models × 4 formats = 16 models total

**Stage 1 (per format):**
- Binary classifier: P(PPG > 2.0) = "fantasy relevant?"
- Training: ALL 5,434 players with inverse propensity weighting
- Output: relevance_prob

**Stage 2 (per format):**
- 3 quantile regressors: q_10, q_50, q_90
- Training: Relevant players weighted by 1/P(relevant)
- Output: ppg_floor, ppg_median, ppg_ceiling

**Combined outputs:**
- bust_prob = 1 - relevance_prob
- starter_prob = relevance_prob × P(PPG > 10 | relevant)
- breakout_prob = relevance_prob × P(PPG > 18 | relevant)

### Database Schema Changes

```sql
CREATE TABLE player_predictions (
    player_id INT,
    scoring_format VARCHAR(20),  -- 'ppr', 'standard', 'half_ppr', 'tep'
    season INT,
    ppg_floor DECIMAL(5,2),
    ppg_median DECIMAL(5,2),
    ppg_ceiling DECIMAL(5,2),
    relevance_prob DECIMAL(4,3),
    bust_prob DECIMAL(4,3),
    breakout_prob DECIMAL(4,3),
    starter_prob DECIMAL(4,3),
    PRIMARY KEY (player_id, scoring_format, season)
);
```

## Component-Based Architecture Decision Point (8:52-8:55 AM EST)

### Taylor's New Direction (8:52 AM)

**Quote:** "Also, let's go with the most elegant and long term solution - component-based prediction"

**Context:** After deciding on 4 separate models (6.5-7 week timeline), Taylor wants to switch to component-based prediction architecture

### Critical Warning Delivered (8:52-8:55 AM)

**Component-Based vs Separate Models Tradeoff:**

**Option A: 4 Separate Models (Current Plan)**
- Architecture: 4 complete models (PPR, Standard, Half-PPR, TEP) predict PPG directly
- Total models: 16 (4 formats × [1 binary + 3 quantile])
- Timeline: 6.5-7 weeks total (+3.5 days from simplified)
- Complexity: Moderate
- Status: Agent currently writing this reconciliation

**Option B: Component-Based (Taylor's New Request)**
- Architecture: Predict 6 components separately (rush yards, rec yards, receptions, rush TDs, rec TDs, 2PT)
- Each component: 3 quantile models (q_10, q_50, q_90)
- Total models: 19 (6 components × 3 quantiles + 1 binary classifier)
- Calculate PPG via formula: (rush_yards × 0.1) + (rec_yards × 0.1) + (receptions × format_multiplier) + (TDs × 6) + ...
- Timeline: **8-9 weeks total** (+7-10 days from simplified)
- Complexity: **HIGH - research-level ML**

**Why Component-Based Takes 2+ Weeks Longer:**
1. Train 19 models (similar to 16, minimal difference)
2. **Error propagation is HARD** - combining 6 uncertain predictions into 1 PPG with proper confidence intervals
3. **Multivariate conformal prediction** - research-level complexity, not standard CQR
4. **Testing complexity** - validate 6 components separately + combined PPG
5. **Edge cases** - negative predictions, impossible combinations, component interactions

**Key Issue:** Component-based puts timeline back to 8-9 weeks, which Taylor originally rejected as "crazy"

### Comparison Table Presented

| Approach | Timeline | Complexity | What You Get |
|----------|----------|------------|--------------|
| Separate Models | 6.5-7 weeks | Moderate | Works, ships faster, 100% market coverage |
| Component-Based | 8-9 weeks | High | More elegant, infinite flexibility, BUT back to original timeline |

### Recommendation Delivered

**Strong recommendation:** Do separate models in Phase 1, component-based in Phase 2

**Rationale:**
- Component-based returns to 8-9 week timeline Taylor rejected
- Error propagation for conformal prediction across 6 components is genuinely hard
- Will spend 2-3 weeks debugging component interactions instead of shipping
- Separate models WORK and ship in 6.5-7 weeks
- Phase 2 migration path: Move to component-based once generating revenue, add interpretability features

**Agent Status:**
- Attempted to kill revision agent (session: 936374f8-5b16-4fd2-8cfb-40d806f30b20)
- Kill failed (unknown target - agent may have already completed or wrong session key)

### Decision Required from Taylor

**Option A:** Stick with separate models
- 6.5-7 weeks, moderate complexity
- Current agent writing reconciliation
- Ships faster, proven approach

**Option B:** Switch to component-based
- 8-9 weeks, high complexity
- Kill current agent, spawn new one for component architecture
- Back to original timeline Taylor rejected

**Status (8:55 AM):** Awaiting Taylor's decision on Option A vs Option B

**Key warning:** "Component-based IS more elegant and flexible long-term. But it's significantly more complex... puts you back at 8-9 weeks (your original 'too long' estimate)"

_Component-based decision point: 2026-03-05 8:52-8:55 AM EST - Taylor requested component-based prediction (most elegant long-term solution), critical warning delivered that this extends timeline from 6.5-7 weeks back to 8-9 weeks due to multivariate conformal prediction complexity and error propagation challenges, strong recommendation to do separate models Phase 1 then migrate to component-based Phase 2 once generating revenue, awaiting Taylor's choice between Option A (separate models 6.5-7 weeks moderate complexity) vs Option B (component-based 8-9 weeks high complexity research-level work)_

### All 3 Agents Complete (9:04-9:07 AM)

**Agent 3: Timeline Planner - COMPLETE (9:04 AM, 5m22s runtime)**
- File: `~/.openclaw/workspace-titlerun/research/component-based-timeline.md`
- **Answer: Can we ship in 6-7 weeks? NO.**

**Realistic timelines:**
- Optimistic (50%): 8.5 weeks (42 active days)
- Most likely: 9.5-10 weeks (48 active days)
- Conservative (90%): 12 weeks (55 active days)
- **Delta vs separate models: +2.5 to +4.5 weeks**

**Where extra time goes:**
1. Multivariate error propagation: +4-6 days (ENTIRELY NEW, research-grade work)
2. Component validation: +3-4 days (384-512 validation cells vs 64)
3. TD model debugging: +1-2 days (zero-inflated, high-variance)

**Reality checks:**
- Actual components: 7-8 (not 6) - need receptions + turnovers separately
- Actual models: 24-27 (not 18)
- Critical path bottleneck: multivariate error propagation (Week 3)
- Scope cuts available: 2PT, turnovers as constant, shared relevance gate (~4 days savings)
- Parallelization saves: 4-6 days wall-clock
- **Included hybrid recommendation:** Ship separate models 6.5 weeks, migrate to components Phase 2

**Agent 2: Multivariate CQR Expert - COMPLETE (9:05 AM, 6m56s runtime)**
- File: `~/.openclaw/workspace-titlerun/research/multivariate-cqr-solution.md` (56KB)
- **CRITICAL FINDING: Problem is SIMPLE, not research-level**

**Recommendation: Option 1 — PPG-Level CQR (Direct Calibration)**

**Key insight:** Don't need multivariate conformal prediction at all
- PPG is deterministic scalar function of 6 components
- Apply standard univariate CQR to combined PPG output
- Calibration step automatically corrects for correlation errors
- Implementation time: **1-2 days (NOT weeks!)**

**Why other options wrong:**
- Multivariate CQR: Overkill, solving harder problem than needed
- Bootstrap: No coverage guarantee, assumes independence
- Quantile arithmetic: Ad-hoc fudge factors

**Critical correction:** Naive sum of component intervals is TOO WIDE (97-99% coverage), not too narrow (50-60%). CQR tightens via negative Q value.

**Deliverable:** Complete `ComponentCQR` class with code skeleton, serialization, per-format calibration (fixes FLAW-C2 from adversarial audit), validation utilities

**Agent 1: Architecture Designer - COMPLETE (9:07 AM, runtime ~12 min)**
- File: `~/.openclaw/workspace-titlerun/research/component-based-architecture-design.md`

**Designed:**
- All 6 component model specifications with features (universal + component-specific + contextual + college, ~19-22 features per component)
- Two-stage decision: **Option C (Neither A nor B)** - No explicit relevance gate, position filtering + sample weighting + quantile regression natural zero-handling replaces classifiers
- **Total models: 18 (not 19-24)**
- Scoring format calculation with quantile combination analysis
- Edge cases: negative predictions (clip to 0), position caps, conservation checks (log-only)
- Feature engineering: Dropped 7 redundant from original 22, added 14 new component-specific
- Database schema: 4 tables (component_predictions, ppg_predictions, cqr_calibration, ppg_breakdown)
- Training pipeline: 8 steps with parallelization (1.5-3 hours total)

**CRITICAL FLAGS:**
1. **QB passing stats NOT covered** - 6 components miss 78% of QB scoring (pass yards, pass TDs, INTs)
2. **2PT nearly unpredictable** - recommend position-average constant (saves 3 models)
3. **Recommended model count: 15** (5 real components + 2PT constant) for Phase 1.1
4. **MUST verify `historical_players` has per-game stat breakdowns** - if only PPG exists, architecture fails at data level

### Summary of Findings (9:07 AM)

**Component-Based Architecture Assessment:**

**Timeline:** 9.5-10 weeks realistic (not 6-7 weeks Taylor hoped)
- +2.5-4.5 weeks vs separate models (6.5-7 weeks)

**Technical complexity:** 
- Multivariate CQR: SOLVED simply (1-2 days, not weeks)
- Component validation: +3-4 days (multiplicatively larger surface area)
- Model count: 18 models (or 15 with scope cuts)

**Critical blockers:**
- QB passing stats missing (78% of QB scoring uncovered)
- Must verify database has per-game stat breakdowns (not just PPG)

**Comparison to separate models:**
- Separate: 6.5-7 weeks, 16 models, proven approach, ships faster
- Component: 9.5-10 weeks, 18 models, elegant but longer, QB gap

**Decision required:** Proceed with component-based (9.5-10 weeks) or return to separate models (6.5-7 weeks)?

_Component-based expert analysis complete: 2026-03-05 8:55-9:07 AM EST - 3 parallel agents delivered comprehensive findings (timeline 9.5-10 weeks realistic +2.5-4.5 weeks vs separate models, multivariate CQR solved simply in 1-2 days not research-level, 18 models with critical QB passing stats gap covering 78% of QB scoring, architecture design complete but must verify database has per-game stat breakdowns, awaiting Taylor's decision to proceed with component-based or return to separate models)_

## Critical Strategic Context: ML System IS The Product (9:15-9:19 AM EST)

### Taylor's Strategic Clarification (9:15 AM)

**Quote:** "Our trade engine, the recommendations, all of it, isn't good enough as it currently stands to warrant delivery. That's why we're building out all of this predictive data and putting together the full picture."

**Context:** After launch date discussion, Taylor clarified why ML system is foundation not add-on

### The Real Picture

**Current TitleRun (deployed at app.titlerun.co):**
- Trade engine exists ✓
- Recommendations exist ✓
- Valuations exist (10-source Bayesian) ✓
- **Status: Not good enough to launch** ✗
- This is prototype/proof-of-concept, NOT launch-ready product

**Component-Based ML System:**
- THIS is what makes recommendations actually valuable
- THIS is what makes trade engine worth using
- THIS is the "full picture" that warrants delivery
- **THIS IS THE PRODUCT** (not an add-on feature)

### Why This Matters

**Without predictive data:**
- Trade recommendations are weak
- Valuations aren't compelling
- No competitive advantage vs KeepTradeCut/DynastyDominator

**With component-based ML system:**
- Proper uncertainty quantification (90% confidence intervals)
- Infinite scoring format flexibility (PPR/Standard/Half-PPR/TEP/custom)
- Component breakdowns (interpretability: "Why is this player ranked here?")
- Future-proof architecture
- **Actually better than competitors**

### Strategic Framing Correction

**OLD FRAMING (WRONG):**
- "ML projections are nice-to-have upgrade feature"
- "Ship April 15 with existing system, add ML later"
- "Existing valuation good enough for launch"

**NEW FRAMING (CORRECT):**
- "ML predictions ARE the product"
- "Current system is prototype, not launch-ready"
- "May 19 is when we have something worth launching"
- "Ship when it's actually good, not when calendar says so"

### Validated Decisions

This strategic context validates all today's decisions:
- ✅ Pushing launch to May 19 (ship when actually good, not rushed)
- ✅ Spending 8-9 weeks on ML (this is core value proposition)
- ✅ Building component-based not separate models (elegant, future-proof)
- ✅ Being aggressive with timeline (want it done right AND fast)
- ✅ Taylor's "I believe in you and the team" (worth the complexity)

### Roadmap Framing Shift

**March 10 - May 12: BUILD THE PRODUCT (9 weeks)**
- Not "adding a feature"
- Building the core value proposition
- Making TitleRun actually competitive

**May 12-19: FINAL POLISH (1 week)**
- Wire good predictions to UI
- Make intelligence shine through
- Polish experience around core value

**May 19: LAUNCH SOMETHING WORTH LAUNCHING**
- Not "we shipped on time"
- "We shipped something actually good"

### Key Insight for All Future Work

**The existing deployed features at app.titlerun.co are proof-of-concept infrastructure, not the product itself.**

The component-based ML system with proper predictions is what makes TitleRun:
1. Worth paying for
2. Better than competitors
3. A business (not just a side project)

This is why Taylor is willing to push launch 5 weeks and spend 8-9 weeks on ML. This is why component-based architecture (despite complexity) is the right choice. This is why "getting it right" matters more than "shipping fast."

**Bottom line:** Don't think of this as "delaying launch." Think of it as "building the actual product" vs shipping a prototype.

**Agent 4: Training Infrastructure**

**Deliverables:**

1. **ComponentCQR class** (~500 lines)
   - File: `src/models/component_cqr.py`
   - Methods: fit_component(), fit_all(), predict_components(), combine_to_ppg(), calibrate(), calibrate_all_formats(), predict_ppg(), predict_component_breakdown(), predict_all_formats(), save(), load(), get_calibration_report(), get_feature_importance()
   - Complete PPG-level CQR implementation with all 4 scoring formats

2. **Training scripts (3 files):**
   - `scripts/train_all_components.py` - Train 24 quantile models (CLI with args)
   - `scripts/calibrate_cqr.py` - Compute Q values per format
   - `scripts/batch_predict.py` - Predict all players → CSV + optional DB write

3. **Key design decisions implemented:**
   - Sample weighting: Three-tier relevance (2.0/1.0/0.3) + recency boost (1.1^years)
   - Tail quantile regularization: q_10/q_90 use more regularization than q_50
   - Position caps: Hard limits prevent extrapolation (RB rush ≤150/game, WR rec ≤120/game, QB pass ≤350/game)
   - CQR at PPG level: Separate Q per format, finite-sample correction applied

### Critical Findings Summary (10:16 AM)

**AUDIT 1: Database Verification - 3 CRITICAL bugs**
1. `team_seasons` table COMPLETELY EMPTY (0 rows) - All team rank features unavailable, must derive from nfl_seasonal_stats
2. Snap data 100% NULL in career_trajectories - Must aggregate from nfl_snap_counts (298K weekly records)
3. Age calculation formula WRONG for 33.4% of rows (Sept-Dec birthdays off by 1 year)
- **4 HIGH issues:** College tier broken (2.1% populated), postseason contamination (dilutes elite players 3-5%), 25.5% missing universal features, position misclassification
- **Verdict:** CANNOT START MONDAY - Need 5-6 hours blocking fixes first
- **Revised prep estimate:** 14-20 hours (not 1.5 hours!)

**AUDIT 2: Feature Engineering SQL - 1 CRITICAL bug**
1. Duplicate pfr_id values in player_id_mapping cause 1 extra row (13,496 vs 13,495) - Fix: DISTINCT ON in snap_data CTE (5 minutes)
- **2 HIGH issues:** Feature count inconsistencies across documentation sections, 3 Blueprint college features impossible (column doesn't exist)
- **Excellent news:** Master CTE query RUNS successfully (218ms, 13,496 rows × 80 columns), zero syntax errors, window functions work correctly, no performance issues
- **Verdict:** SQL can run Monday after 5-minute fix ✅

**AUDIT 3: Training Scripts & DevOps - 2 CRITICAL blockers**
1. pyarrow missing from requirements.txt (1-minute fix)
2. No extract_features.py script - Pipeline has no Step 1!
- **3 HIGH issues:** config/ directory is dead code (never imported), version hardcoded in calibrate_cqr.py, path mismatch (features/ vs features.parquet)
- **4 MEDIUM issues:** No feature column validation, redundant predict_ppg call, password not URL-encoded, validate_coverage.py stub
- **4 LOW issues:** All tests placeholders, PPG ceiling hardcoded, no .env warning, 8 stub source files
- **Excellent news:** Ran full pipeline (train → calibrate → predict) with synthetic data - IT WORKS! ComponentCQR class solid (~550 lines real code), CQR math correct
- **Verdict:** Can train Monday IF pyarrow added (1 min) and features.parquet created (1-8 hours) ✅

**AUDIT 4: ComponentCQR Python - 2 CRITICAL bugs**
1. **Inverted recency weighting** (line 214) - `1.1^(2024 - season)` gives 2000 data 10× MORE weight than 2024, exact opposite of intent (bug from blueprint spec itself)
2. No input validation in fit_component() - Empty arrays crash, all-NaN targets produce garbage models
- **4 HIGH bugs:** Floor > ceiling after CQR correction (negative Q with narrow intervals), partial model loading KeyError, fit_all() doesn't check y_val_components, NaN propagation in calibrate() corrupts all predictions
- **3 MEDIUM bugs:** INT quantile not flipped (wastes ~3.6 PPG precision for QBs), approximate finite-sample correction, silent Q=0 fallback
- **3 LOW bugs:** Unused games parameter, unused two_pt_constant attribute, no unknown position warning
- **Code quality:** GOOD - All 13+ promised methods exist and implemented, well-structured, correct CQR math (minus recency bug)
- **Verdict:** Can train Monday AFTER Block 1 fixes (~1 hour of coding)

### Overall Audit Summary (10:16 AM)

**Total bugs found across all 4 audits:** 30+
- **8 CRITICAL bugs** (2 database, 1 SQL, 2 DevOps, 2 Python)
- **13 HIGH bugs**
- **7 MEDIUM bugs**
- **7 LOW bugs**

**Fix time estimates:**

### ComponentCQR Fixes Summary (10:28 AM)

**All 12 bugs fixed with 53 unit tests passing:**

**2 CRITICAL:**
1. Inverted recency weighting - Old data now decays correctly (was boosted 10× by mistake)
2. Input validation - Added to fit_component(), fit_all(), predict_ppg()

**4 HIGH:**
3. Floor > ceiling bug - Crossing intervals collapse to midpoint
4. Partial model loading - Graceful zeros + completeness validation
5. fit_all() key check - Validates all component keys exist
6. NaN propagation - Filters NaN, enforces ≥20 valid samples in calibrate()

**3 MEDIUM:**
7. INT quantile flip - Negative components flip q_10↔q_90 (fewer INTs = better)
8. Finite-sample correction - Exact formula: ⌈(n+1)×α⌉/n
9. Q=0 fallback - Now raises ValueError if format not calibrated

**3 LOW:**
10. Unused games parameter - Removed from combine_to_ppg()
11. Unused two_pt_constant - Removed from __init__()
12. Unknown position - Logs warning for unrecognized positions

**Breaking API changes:**
- combine_to_ppg(): games parameter removed
- predict_ppg(): Raises if format uncalibrated (add allow_uncalibrated=True for old behavior)
- fit_all(): Requires ALL component keys in train/val dicts
- load(): Validates completeness (incomplete dirs raise error)

**Test coverage: 53 comprehensive tests, ALL PASSING** ✅

## Full ML Training Complete: All 24 Models Trained (10:45 AM - 11:02 AM EST)

### Training Agent Completion (11:02 AM, 17-minute runtime)

**Agent:** train-all-components
- Session: `agent:researcher:subagent:8e79cf03-19dc-40da-aa1e-fc5d6b64d622`
- Runtime: 17 minutes (started 10:45 AM, completed 11:02 AM)
- Timeout: 4 hours (completed WAY ahead of schedule)
- File: `TRAINING_COMPLETE_REPORT.md`

### All 24 Models Trained Successfully ✅

**Training completed:** 8 components × 3 quantiles = 24 LightGBM models
- rush_yards, rec_yards, receptions, rush_td, rec_td, pass_yards, pass_td, pass_int
- Each component: q_10, q_50, q_90 quantile models
- Training data: 11,771 player-seasons (2000-2021)
- Validation data: 591 player-seasons (2022)
- Total training time: ~25 seconds (all 24 models)
- Features used: 67 per component (after leakage fix)

### CRITICAL BUG DISCOVERED AND FIXED 🐛

**Severe data leakage found:**
- 8 current-season stat columns (`*_pg`) were exact copies of target variables
- Correlation = 1.000 (perfect correlation)
- Made initial model appear suspiciously accurate (0.5 PPG intervals, near-perfect predictions)
- **Root cause:** extract_features.py included both `rush_yards_per_game` (target) AND `rush_yards_pg` (feature) as separate columns

**Fix applied:**
- Removed all `*_pg` leakage columns from feature sets
- Fixed in: train_all_components.py, calibrate_cqr.py, batch_predict.py, validate_coverage.py
- Re-trained all models with clean feature sets
- Models now using only legitimate prior-season and universal features

**Impact:** Predictions went from unrealistically precise (0.5 PPG intervals) to realistic (~10-15 PPG intervals), maintaining interpretability

### Calibration Complete ✅

**All 4 scoring formats calibrated:**
- PPR: Q = +0.876 (widens intervals)
- Standard: Q = +0.519
- Half-PPR: Q = +0.609
- TEP: Q = +0.933

**Calibration data:** 2023 season (583 player-seasons)

### Coverage Validation Results (2024 Test Set)

**Overall coverage (slightly under target):**
| Format | Coverage | Target | Pass? |
|--------|----------|--------|-------|
| PPR | 89.2% | ≥90% | ⚠️ Close (0.8% short) |
| Standard | 89.3% | ≥90% | ⚠️ Close (0.7% short) |
| Half-PPR | 87.2% | ≥90% | ❌ Miss (2.8% short) |
| TEP | 88.8% | ≥90% | ⚠️ Close (1.2% short) |

**Position breakdown:**
- QB: 90.1% (meets target) ✅
- RB: 93.0-96.5% (exceeds target) ✅
- WR: 82.0-85.0% (primary shortfall) ❌
- TE: 88.0-92.0% (close) ⚠️

**Root cause:** WRs are most volatile position (high TD variance, target-dependent production)

## Data Coverage Issue Discovered & Re-Training Initiated (11:02-11:07 AM EST)

### Critical Discovery: Missing Recent Data (11:02 AM)

**Taylor's question:** "Did we include all of 2025's data in this? Let's move forward with your recommended next steps but want to ensure we're up to date on the latest data"

**Investigation revealed TWO problems:**

**Problem 1: Training didn't use all available data**
- Initial training used: 2000-2021 (stopped 4 years ago!)
- Available in features.parquet: 2000-2024 (13,495 rows)
- **Wasted 3 years of available data** (2022-2024 not used in training)

**Problem 2: 2025 data missing from database**
- features.parquet only has data through 2024
- 2025 season (just finished Feb 2026) not in database yet
- Cannot predict 2026 season without 2025 data as "prior year"

**Data availability check:**
```
Season range in features.parquet: 2000-2024
Total rows: 13,495
2025 data: 0 rows
```

**Impact:**
- Features like `prior_rush_yards_pg` pulling from 2020-2021 (5 years old!)
- Missing most recent 3-4 years of NFL evolution
- Cannot make 2026 predictions (which was the goal) - can only predict 2025

### Re-Training Agent Deployed (11:05 AM)

**Agent:** retrain-with-2024-data
- Session: `agent:researcher:subagent:23e232f0-ab08-42a0-87b3-920c4825e62f`
- Model: Opus
- Timeout: 90 minutes (5,400 seconds)
- ETA: ~12:35 PM

**Mission:** Re-train with complete dataset + apply all 4 priority improvements

**Correct data split:**
- Train: 2000-2023 (~12,500 rows) - uses ALL available training data
- Validation: 2024 (70% of 2024 data)
- Calibration: 2024 (30% of 2024 data)
- Test: Held-out 2023 subset for coverage validation

**4 Priority Improvements Being Applied:**

1. **Position-Specific CQR Calibration (Priority 1)**
   - Old: 1 Q per format (4 total)
   - New: 1 Q per format × per position (16 total: PPR_QB, PPR_RB, PPR_WR, PPR_TE, etc.)
   - Expected impact: WR coverage 82-85% → 90%+

2. **Per-Component Feature Selection (Priority 2)**
   - Old: 67 features for all components (too broad)
   - New: 19-22 features per component (from FEATURE_ENGINEERING_SPEC.md canonical sets)
   - Expected impact: More targeted models, less noise

3. **Position-Filtered Training (Priority 3)**
   - Old: All positions for all components (trained pass_yards on RBs!)
   - New: Only relevant positions per component (QBs for passing, RBs+QBs for rushing, WRs/RBs/TEs for receiving)
   - Expected impact: More focused, higher-quality models

4. **Leakage Verification (Priority 4)**
   - Double-check no `*_pg` columns as features (only as targets)
   - Ensure clean feature sets

**Target outcomes:**
- ≥90% coverage for ALL positions (including WRs)
- Models trained on most recent available data
- 2025 predictions ready (best we can do without 2025 database data)

### Clarification: 2025 vs 2026 Predictions (11:05 AM)

**What we CAN predict right now:**
- 2025 season (using 2024 as "prior year" data)
- This is the most recent we can predict with current database

**What we CANNOT predict yet:**
- 2026 season (requires 2025 stats in database as "prior year")
- 2025 data doesn't exist in database yet (season just finished Feb 2026)

**To enable 2026 predictions (future task):**
1. Update database with 2025 season stats
2. Re-run extract_features.py (will include 2025)
3. Re-train one more time (train 2000-2024, validate 2025)
4. Predict 2026 (using 2025 as prior year)

**Current plan:** Generate best-possible 2025 predictions today, then update database with 2025 data as separate task for true 2026 predictions

## V3 Adversarial Audit Complete: Model Sound, Data Pipeline Needs Fixes (11:30 AM - 12:01 PM EST)

### Taylor's Request for Adversarial Audit (11:28 AM)

**Quote:** "Can we audit what was just run with a group of expert adversarial sub agents on opus?"

**Context:** After v3 training completed with 94% coverage claim, Taylor requested rigorous adversarial audit (same proven workflow that found 30+ bugs this morning)

**Deployment:** 4 adversarial agents, all on Opus, running in parallel (11:30 AM start)

### All 4 Audits Complete (11:30 AM - 12:01 PM, ~15 minutes total)

**Agent 1: Training Methodology & Code Quality** (12:01 PM, 31m runtime)
- Session: `agent:researcher:subagent:3eff8ca0-0250-4fc6-8480-be4b344287cc`
- File: `AUDIT_V3_METHODOLOGY.md`
- Verdict: **CONDITIONAL PASS** (0 Critical, 2 High, 3 Medium, 3 Low)

**Agent 2: Predictions Quality & Realism** (11:43 PM, 13m runtime)
- Session: `agent:researcher:subagent:3d5417c5-4d3c-48bb-8a8f-a9d20051e05c`
- File: `AUDIT_V3_PREDICTIONS.md`
- Verdict: **REALISTIC with 2 critical data pipeline issues**

**Agent 3: Data Quality & Feature Engineering** (11:45 PM, 15m runtime)
- Session: `agent:researcher:subagent:b13a384a-c4e3-408e-996d-9a2639d78032`
- File: `AUDIT_V3_DATA_QUALITY.md`
- Verdict: **3 CRITICAL issues, 3 HIGH issues**

**Agent 4: Coverage Validation Methodology** (11:44 PM, 14m runtime)
- Session: `agent:researcher:subagent:89402367-7389-4f54-a2ed-2b53df85a4bc`
- File: `AUDIT_V3_COVERAGE_VALIDATION.md`
- Verdict: **94% coverage claim VERIFIED - accept with caveats**

### Critical Findings Summary

**✅ WHAT'S WORKING (Model & Methodology):**
1. **94% coverage claim is VERIFIED** - Reproduced exactly, 0.0% difference across all 16 position×format combinations
2. **No coverage inflation bugs** - No sample exclusion, no NaN issues, no cherry-picking
3. **CQR methodology sound** - Follows Romano et al. 2019 correctly, proper held-out calibration
4. **Train/val split clean** - Zero overlap, 2025 never in training, no leakage
5. **Recency weighting correct** - Recent seasons get 10× more weight (NOT inverted)
6. **Position filters correct** - Applied before training, correct positions per component
7. **Elite player rankings realistic** - Fantasy expert smell test passed
8. **Format consistency perfect** - Zero violations across 2,464 predictions
9. **Samples-per-feature healthy** - All components >90:1 ratio (lowest: pass_int at 106:1)
10. **Lag features correct** - 955 pairs checked, 0 mismatches

**🔴 CRITICAL ISSUES FOUND (Data Pipeline - 6 total):**

**From Training Methodology Audit:**
1. **Predictions use stale features** (HIGH, not CRITICAL)
   - "2026 predictions" actually use 2024 prior-season data (not 2025)
   - Verified: `prior_rush_yards_pg` in 2025 rows exactly equals 2024 `rush_yards_per_game`
   - Misleading code comment claims "2025 stats"
   - Coverage validation is valid (uses 2025 data correctly)
   - **Fix:** Re-run feature engineering to create proper 2026 rows with 2025 priors
   - **Impact:** Predictions miss most recent season of player performance

2. **`np.nan_to_num(nan=0.0)` defeats LightGBM's native NaN handling** (HIGH)
   - Features with 35-64% NaN rates imputed to 0.0 (false semantic meaning)
   - Affects: height_inches, prior_snap_pct, prior_rush_td_rate, etc.
   - LightGBM can route NaN to optimal child nodes (strictly better)
   - **Fix:** Remove `nan_to_num` calls for feature matrices
   - **Impact:** Reduces model discriminative power

**From Data Quality Audit:**
3. **`np.nan_to_num(X, nan=0.0)` in train_v3.py** (CRITICAL - duplicate of #2 above)
   - Contradicts spec's "let LightGBM handle NaN natively" strategy
   - height=0 for 23% of rows, snap_pct=0 for 62%, all rookie priors=0
   - Single highest-impact fix

4. **`prior_pass_rating` is 100% NULL with `object` dtype** (CRITICAL)
   - Completely broken feature in pass_yards model
   - After nan_to_num becomes all-zeros column (dead feature)
   - **Fix:** Fix data type or remove feature

5. **`handle_nans()` spec function was never applied** (CRITICAL)
   - Parquet has 23.3% NULL height, 6.3% NULL weight, 7.2% NULL age
   - Spec defined targeted imputation, DB Fixes claimed 0% NULL
   - **Fix:** Apply handle_nans() function from spec before training

6. **Negative stat values in source data** (CRITICAL from Predictions Audit)
   - 21 players with negative rush yards/game (physically impossible)
   - 490 rows with negative college rushing yards
   - 891 rows with negative air yards
   - Indicates data contamination (likely sack yardage leaking into rushing stats)
   - **Fix:** Clean source data, verify nflverse import logic

**From Predictions Quality Audit:**
7. **Philip Rivers ghost player** (CRITICAL)
   - Retired in 2020 but appears with fabricated 2025 stats (3 games, 181 pass yds/g)
   - Gets 15.8 PPG median prediction for 2026
   - 19 total players have 3+ year career gaps
   - **Fix:** Filter out retired/inactive players from 2025 dataset

8. **Old/retired player predictions** (HIGH)
   - Aaron Rodgers (41, 16.8 PPG), Joe Flacco (40, 15.5 PPG), Marcedes Lewis (41, 4.8 PPG)
   - All get predictions despite questionable NFL status
   - **Fix:** Add age/activity filters

**🟡 HIGH ISSUES (Non-Critical):**
- QB interval widths not personalized (all ~20-21 PPG wide due to small calibration set n=25)
- Height NULL pattern creates era bias (48% NULL for 2000-2010 → model learns height=0 as "old player")
- Zero-stat players lower overall coverage to 81.6% (excluding them raises to 95.7%)

**⚠️ MEDIUM ISSUES:**
- Asymmetric miss pattern (22 below-floor vs 2 above-ceiling) due to floor clipping at 0 PPG
- QB coverage (91.5%) not individually statistically significant above 90% (small sample)
- Excess coverage (94% vs 90% target) suggests intervals could be tighter

### Audit Methodology & Results

**Same proven workflow from this morning:**
- This morning: 4 adversarial agents found 30+ bugs before v1 training
- All bugs fixed → production-ready foundation
- Now: Same rigor applied to v3 post-training

**Coverage verification methodology:**
- Independent reproduction of coverage calculation
- Zero difference found (exact match)
- No bugs in calculation
- Calibration (n=185) and validation (n=431) properly separated
- No NaN values in validation data
- No sample exclusion detected

**Key distinction:**
- **Model quality:** Excellent (94% coverage verified, methodology sound)
- **Data quality:** Critical issues (ghost players, negative stats, NaN handling, stale features)

### Recommendations from Audits

**Training Methodology Audit:**
- Ship the model as-is for internal use
- Fix feature pipeline for accurate 2026 predictions before external publication
- Priority: HIGH (not blocking internal use, but needed for production)

**Predictions Quality Audit:**
- Model is good, data pipeline needs fixes before production deployment
- Priority: CRITICAL (affects prediction accuracy)

**Data Quality Audit:**
- Apply handle_nans() function from spec
- Remove np.nan_to_num calls
- Fix prior_pass_rating dtype
- Clean negative stat values from source
- Priority: CRITICAL (affects model training quality)

- Priority: No blocking issues

### Action Items Before Production

## V4 Clean Data Pipeline Complete: All 6 Critical Fixes Implemented (12:01-12:17 PM EST)

### Taylor's Decision to Fix All Issues First (12:01 PM)

**Quote:** "Let's have an expert opus subagent implement all fixes before we move forward"

**Context:** After reviewing all 4 adversarial audit reports showing 6 critical data pipeline issues, Taylor chose to fix everything properly before moving to integration (quality over speed approach)

**Rejected alternatives:**
- Using v3 as-is for internal testing
- Hybrid approach (integrate v3 while fixing in parallel)

**Strategic decision:** Ship quality - fix all data pipeline issues comprehensively, then move forward with confidence

### Comprehensive Fix Agent Deployed (12:03 PM)

**Agent:** fix-data-pipeline-train-v4
- Session: `agent:researcher:subagent:d068d24d-8bb9-487e-a272-e797b3a7a6ee`
- Model: Opus
- Timeout: 90 minutes
- Actual runtime: 14 minutes (completed 12:17 PM)
- Expected: 60-90 minutes, finished 76 minutes early

**Mission:** Implement ALL 6 critical fixes from adversarial audits, then train production-ready v4 model

### All 6 Critical Fixes Implemented (12:03-12:17 PM)

**FIX 1: 2026 Features with 2025 Priors** ✅
- **Problem:** "2026 predictions" used 2024 priors (stale by 1 year)
- **Solution:** Created 616 proper 2026 rows where `prior_*` features come from 2025 actual stats
- **Verification:** Per-player spot checks (Josh Allen's prior_pass_yards matches 2025 actual)
- **Impact:** Predictions now use most recent season data (2025 instead of 2024)

**FIX 2: Applied handle_nans() Function** ✅
- **Problem:** Spec defined targeted imputation but was never applied (23.3% NULL height, 6.3% NULL weight, 7.2% NULL age)
- **Solution:** Implemented spec's targeted imputation strategy
  - Age: 1,013 NULLs → 0 via `22 + experience` formula
  - Height: 3,502 NULLs → 0 via position median
  - Weight: 885 NULLs → 0 via position median
  - Lagged/rate/college features: left as NaN for LightGBM native handling
- **Impact:** Proper imputation instead of blanket 0.0 replacement

**FIX 3: Removed np.nan_to_num** ✅
- **Problem:** Code replaced ALL NaN with 0.0, defeating LightGBM's native NaN handling
- **Solution:** Removed all `np.nan_to_num` calls from feature matrices
- **Implementation:** LightGBM now handles NaN natively (can route to optimal child nodes)
- **Exception:** Targets retain zero-fill (legitimate - missing targets = 0 production)
- **Impact:** Model can properly learn from missing data patterns

**FIX 4: Dropped prior_pass_rating** ✅
- **Problem:** 100% NULL with object dtype, dead feature in pass_yards model
- **Solution:** Removed from pass_yards feature set (21 → 20 features)
- **Impact:** No more dead feature wasting model capacity

**FIX 5: Cleaned Negative Stats** ✅
- **Problem:** 3,097+ physically impossible negative values (rush yards, college stats, air yards, etc.)
- **Solution:** Clipped to 0 across 7 features
  - College stats: negative values → 0
  - Air yards: negative values → 0
  - Team shares: negative values → 0
  - NFL negatives kept (legitimate - e.g., sack yards)
- **Impact:** Data integrity improved, no more impossible values

**FIX 6: Filtered Ghost/Retired Players** ✅
- **Problem:** 19 players with 3+ year career gaps getting predictions (Philip Rivers retired 2020, etc.)
- **Solution:** Removed 6 players
  - Philip Rivers (retired 2020, fabricated 2025 stats)
  - Marcedes Lewis (age 41)
  - 4 others with career gaps + minimal activity
- **Filters applied:**
  - Career gaps ≥3 years
  - Age >40 for non-QB, >42 for QB
  - Minimal recent activity
- **Impact:** 616 → 610 active player predictions (6 ghost players removed)

### 3 of 4 Audits Complete (12:44-12:46 PM, 3-5 minute runtimes)

**Agent 1: API Endpoints Audit Complete** (12:44 PM, 3m40s runtime)
- File: `AUDIT_API_ENDPOINTS.md`
- Runtime: 3 minutes 40 seconds (26 minutes under estimate)

**2 CRITICAL issues:**
1. **playerIdMapping routes are DEAD CODE** - Route file exists with 4 endpoints but never mounted in `index.js` (completely inaccessible)
2. **Prediction endpoints have ZERO authentication** - All 4 endpoints fully public, anyone can scrape 2,440 predictions with no auth token

**5 HIGH issues:**
- No endpoint-specific rate limiting (only global 500/15min)
- Position rankings query fetches ALL 610 rows then filters in JavaScript (should filter in SQL)
- Duplicated WHERE clause logic between data query and count query (maintenance hazard)
- Inconsistent response formats between route files (`sendSuccess` envelope vs raw `res.json`)
- Zero tests for any of the 8 endpoints

**6 MEDIUM issues:**
- No CHECK constraints on ml_predictions table (no floor≤median≤ceiling enforcement, no NOT NULL, no position/format validation)
- No foreign key between ml_predictions and prediction_player_mappings (different types: VARCHAR vs INTEGER)
- player_id semantics confused (docs say Sleeper ID but likely internal ML model ID)
- Logger inconsistency (Pino structured vs printf-style)
- Silent failure in nested query catch block
- Missing sleeperId validation in playerIdMapping route

**Good findings:**
- SQL injection protection solid (all parameterized queries)
- CORS properly configured
- Caching well-implemented
- Code clean and well-organized

**Verdict:** NEEDS FIXES before production (2-4 hours to address critical/high items)

**Agent 4: Integration Tests Audit Complete** (12:45 PM, 4m19s runtime)
- File: `AUDIT_INTEGRATION_TESTS.md`
- Runtime: 4 minutes 19 seconds (25 minutes under estimate)

**3 CRITICAL issues:**
1. **Tests validate cached outputs, not live computation** - Core 9 coverage/metrics tests read from JSON file, don't run actual validation pipeline
2. **Zero error-path tests** - No tests for missing files, corrupt data, or failure scenarios
3. **Three placeholder test files** - `test_features.py`, `test_prediction.py`, `test_training.py` contain only `assert True`

**Positive findings:**
- 55 tests are real and meaningful (not trivial)
- Assertions check specific numeric thresholds, data relationships, domain invariants
- `test_component_cqr.py` (53 unit tests) is excellent - real mocks, bug-fix coverage, edge cases
- Domain-aware assertions (PPR > standard for receivers, floor ≤ median ≤ ceiling across all rows)
- Validation script itself well-written and trustworthy on code review
- Model metrics genuinely strong (96.3% coverage, 2.93 MAE, 0.803 correlation verified)

**Architectural flaw:** Tests validate pre-computed output files rather than running actual validation pipeline - if someone edits results JSON or validation script has bug, all 55 tests still pass

**Verdict:** Ship the model, but add ~15 more tests (end-to-end prediction, error paths, process verification) before relying on suite as automated quality gate

**Agent 2: UI Components Audit Complete** (12:46 PM, 5m21s runtime)
- File: `AUDIT_UI_COMPONENTS.md`
- Runtime: 5 minutes 21 seconds (24 minutes under estimate)

**4 CRITICAL issues (accessibility violations):**
1. **RankingsTable sort headers NOT keyboard accessible** - `<th onClick>` with no `tabIndex`, `role`, `onKeyDown`, or `aria-sort` (WCAG 2.1.1 Level A violation)
2. **Chart SVG has no accessible name** - Recharts `<BarChart>` renders SVG invisible to screen readers (WCAG 1.1.1 Level A violation)
3. **text-gray-600 on dark backgrounds fails 4.5:1 contrast** - Affects footer text, range values, legends across multiple files (WCAG 1.4.3 AA violation)
4. **SortHeader defined INSIDE RankingsTable** - React anti-pattern that re-creates component type on every render, causing full unmount/remount of `<th>` elements and focus loss

**7 HIGH issues:**
- ErrorBar in chart only shows ceiling (upside), not floor - half the uncertainty data missing from visualization
- No empty states for 0 predictions
- No NaN/Infinity guards on `.toFixed()` calls
- Duplicate query key factories (`predictionKeys` in hook vs `queryKeys.predictions` in central file) - cache coherence bug waiting to happen
- `refetchOnWindowFocus` not disabled for slowly-changing prediction data
- Filter buttons lack `aria-pressed`, touch targets undersized
- Range bar always 100% wide regardless of actual range - visually misleading

**8 MEDIUM + 6 LOW issues identified**

**Fix time estimate:** 7-10 hours total (2-3h critical, 3-4h high priority, 2-3h nice-to-have)

**Verdict:** NEEDS FIXES before ship (4 WCAG violations are blockers)

- Added `optionalAuth` import from `../middleware/auth` in `src/routes/predictions.js`
- Applied `optionalAuth` to all 4 prediction endpoints (before `cacheResponse`)
- Middleware chain: `optionalAuth → cacheResponse → handler`
- Non-breaking: anonymous access still works, authenticated users get `req.user` attached
- Matches pattern already used in `playerIdMapping.js`

### Complete UI Information Display Review (2:27-2:29 PM)

**Component 1: PredictionCard (Individual Player Display)**

**Information hierarchy:**
1. **Header** - Position badge (QB/RB/WR/TE), player name, team, position rank (with trophy icon)
2. **Hero number** - Median PPG (4xl font, white, most prominent), format label, trending indicator (up/down arrow with +/- value)
3. **Visual range bar** - Gradient bar showing full range, white marker at median, three numbers (floor, median, ceiling)
4. **Context** - Uncertainty level (Low/Medium/High with color), range size in PPG, starter threshold (green/gray dot), model version footer

**Key features:**
- Median PPG is clear focal point
- Risk shown visually (range bar) and numerically (floor/ceiling)
- Starter threshold provides actionable context
- Trending shows momentum
- WCAG 2.1 AA compliant (role="meter" with ARIA, proper contrast)

**Component 2: RankingsTable (All Players List)**

**Information display:**
- **Filter bar** - Position filters (ALL/QB/RB/WR/TE), player count
- **Sortable columns** - #, Player, Pos, Median PPG (bold), Floor, Ceiling, Range, Trend
- **Interactive** - Click headers to sort, click rows for detail, keyboard accessible
- **Responsive** - Range column hidden on mobile
- **Bottom legend** - Starter thresholds for each position

**Key features:**
- All 6 column headers fully keyboard accessible (tabIndex, role, onKeyDown, aria-sort)
- Position filters with aria-pressed
- Clean visual hierarchy
- Trend arrows color-coded
- WCAG 2.1 AA compliant

**Component 3: PredictionComparison (Format Comparison)**

**Information display:**
- **Bar chart** - 4 bars (PPR, Standard, Half PPR, TEP), error bars showing range, Y-axis labeled "Points Per Game", hover tooltip with all values
- **Data table** - Format, Median PPG, Floor PPG, Ceiling PPG, Range (all in columns)

**Key features:**
- Chart wrapped in role="img" with descriptive aria-label
- Screen-reader-only text alternative listing all data points
- Visual + tabular presentation (different user preferences)
- Shows how format affects value (e.g., PPR higher for receivers)
- WCAG 2.1 AA compliant

### Information Quality Assessment

**Overall rating: 8.5/10** - Excellent information hierarchy and accessibility

**Strengths identified:**
1. Clear hierarchy - Hero number (median PPG) most prominent, range/uncertainty secondary, context available but not overwhelming
2. Risk communication - Floor/ceiling clearly shown, uncertainty color-coded, visual range bar intuitive
3. Actionable context - Starter threshold helps draft decisions, position rank provides context, trending shows momentum, format comparison valuable
4. Accessibility - Fully keyboard navigable, screen reader compatible, high contrast (5.9:1 ratio)

### 5 Critical Questions Posed to Taylor

**Question 1: Terminology - "Median PPG" vs "Projected PPG"**
- Current: "20.05 PPG (PPR)"
- Alternative: "Projected 20.05 PPG (PPR)"
- Consideration: Does average user understand "median" vs "projected"?

**Question 2: Uncertainty Level Display**
- Current: "Low uncertainty (8.5 PPG range)"
- Alternative: Just show range without low/medium/high labeling
- Consideration: Does "uncertainty" sound negative/concerning to users?

**Question 3: Statistical Interval vs Simple Range**
- Current: Shows floor/ceiling/median (simple)
- Alternative: "90% chance between 10.2 - 18.8 PPG" (statistically accurate)
- Consideration: More accurate but might confuse non-technical users

**Question 4: Trending Indicator Data Source**
- Current: Shows +/- change with up/down arrow
- Question: Is this actually calculated from real data or placeholder?
- Consideration: If not real data, should remove to avoid misleading users

**Question 5: Starter Threshold Communication**
- Current: Green/gray dot with "Starter" / "Below threshold" text
- Alternative: Bucket-style labels like "Top-12 QB" / "QB15-QB24"
- Consideration: Threshold explanation provided in legend (bottom of table)
