## Critical UI Design Feedback - User Journey Missing (2:34-2:51 PM EST)

### Taylor's Honest Assessment (2:34 PM)

**Quote:** "Have to be honest, this is terrible. How does this fit into the full player profile what information is actually important for the user to glean from this?"

**Critical insight:** UI components built in vacuum without understanding:
- User journey (where/when they see predictions)
- Decision context (what problem they're solving)
- Information hierarchy (what matters most)
- Integration points (how it fits into existing TitleRun pages)

**Root cause identified:** Built for data display, not user decision-making

### Fundamental Design Flaw Acknowledged (2:34-2:51 PM)

**Jeff's response:** "You're absolutely right. I built these in a vacuum without thinking about the actual user journey."

**Problem:** 3 UI components (PredictionCard, RankingsTable, PredictionComparison) designed without knowing:
- WHERE users see predictions (player profile? rankings page? trade analyzer? draft board?)
- WHAT DECISION they're making (draft? trade? start/sit? dynasty value?)
- WHAT CONTEXT EXISTS (do they already see game logs, news, trade fairness scores?)
- WHAT'S MOST IMPORTANT (the number? the risk? the trend? the rank?)

### 4 Critical Questions for User-Centered Redesign (2:51 PM)

**Question 1: WHERE does the user see ML predictions?**
- Player profile page? (drilling into specific player)
- Rankings page? (comparing many players)
- Trade analyzer? (evaluating trade offers)
- Draft board? (making draft picks)
- All of the above?

**Question 2: WHAT DECISION is the user trying to make?**
- "Should I draft this player?"
- "Is this trade fair?"
- "Should I start this player?"
- "Who's a better dynasty asset?"

**Question 3: WHAT DO THEY ALREADY KNOW?**
- Are they looking at a player profile that already has:
  - Recent game logs?
  - News/injuries?
  - Existing trade fairness score?
  - Roster context (their team)?

**Question 4: WHAT'S THE SINGLE MOST IMPORTANT THING?**
- The number itself? (20.05 PPG)
- The confidence/risk? (floor/ceiling range)
- The trend? (up/down arrow)
- The rank? (QB1 vs QB12)

### Working Hypothesis (Pending Taylor Confirmation)

**Jeff's guess:**
- Users don't care about "uncertainty" or "floor/ceiling" vocabulary
- They care about: "Is this player good?" and "How risky is this pick?"
- This should probably be ONE LINE in existing player profile, not whole card
- Format comparison only useful in specific contexts (league import)

**Key insight:** The difference between "technically correct data display" and "solves user's actual problem"

**Status at 2:51 PM:** UI design on hold, awaiting Taylor's answers to 4 critical context questions before proceeding with user-centered redesign

**Lesson learned:** Always start with user journey, not data schema. Technical completeness ≠ user value.

_UI design pivot: 2026-03-05 2:34-2:51 PM EST - Taylor's critical feedback exposed fundamental flaw (built in vacuum without user journey), acknowledged design failure, posed 4 critical questions (WHERE/WHAT/CONTEXT/PRIORITY) to understand actual use case, current UI components may need complete rethink based on real user decision-making needs, waiting for Taylor's context before redesigning_


## ML Predictions True Purpose Revealed - Trade Trust Building (2:51-4:05 PM EST)

### Taylor's Critical Context (2:51 PM)

**Quote:** "The context of these ml predictions will initially be in the context of trying to make a better trade experience for both parties. Trades in fantasy usually fall through or get blocked by someone thinking they're not getting a fair deal. I want to use our data/machine learning/algorithms to help each party in the trade understand the future potential impact of the players & picks involved in the trade."

**THE REAL PROBLEM:**
- Trades fall through because one party thinks it's not fair
- Lack of trust in valuations causes friction
- Both parties need to see future value, not just current stats

**THE SOLUTION:**
- ML predictions show future potential of traded players
- Algorithm finds "equal" trades based on projected value
- Data layer provides insights into player upside/risk
- **Goal:** Build trust so both parties feel good about the trade

**Critical insight:** This is NOT about player profiles or league rankings - it's about **trust in trade negotiations**

### Jeff's Understanding Pivot (2:51-4:05 PM)

**Wrong components built:**
- ❌ Individual player cards (PredictionCard.tsx) - wrong context
- ❌ League-wide rankings (RankingsTable.tsx) - wrong context  
- ❌ Format comparison (PredictionComparison.tsx) - wrong context

**Right context - Trade Analyzer:**
```
YOU GIVE:                    YOU GET:
Bijan Robinson (RB)          Ja'Marr Chase (WR)
19.4 PPG projected           19.2 PPG projected
"Safe" (narrow range)        "Boom/Bust" (wide range)

FUTURE VALUE: -0.2 PPG (slightly favor them)
RISK PROFILE: Trading safety for upside
MUTUAL BENEFIT: ✅ Both teams improve positionally
```

### 4 New Critical Questions for Trade Context (4:05 PM)

**Question 1: WHAT'S THE FLOW?**
- User proposes trade → System shows ML predictions → Both parties see future value comparison?
- When does ML prediction appear? (during trade proposal? after submission? in trade review?)

**Question 2: WHAT BUILDS TRUST?**
- Net PPG difference? ("You gain +2.5 PPG in this trade")
- Risk transparency? ("You're giving up consistency for upside")
- Mutual benefit score? ("This helps both teams")
- Historical accuracy badge? ("Our model was 96% accurate last season")

**Question 3: WHAT DO THEY NEED TO SEE?**
- Just bottom line? ("Fair trade - you gain 0.5 PPG")
- Player-by-player breakdown? (see each player's projection)
- Confidence levels? ("High confidence: 90% chance this player outperforms")
- Risk comparison? (safe vs boom/bust)

**Question 4: HOW DOES IT INTEGRATE WITH EXISTING TRADE FAIRNESS?**
- TitleRun already has trade fairness score - does ML just power that?
- Or is this separate "future value" view alongside current value?
- Do both metrics show together? (current fairness + future projection)

### Key Design Principles Identified

**Trust-building requires:**
1. **Transparency** - Show WHY the trade is fair (not just "it's fair")
2. **Mutual benefit** - Both parties see their gain (not zero-sum)
3. **Risk clarity** - Trading upside for safety? Make it explicit
4. **Credibility** - Show model accuracy/confidence to build trust
5. **Simplicity** - Bottom-line takeaway, details on demand

**User psychology insight:** The goal isn't perfect accuracy - it's making both parties feel confident enough to execute the trade

### Next Action Required (4:05 PM)

**Jeff's question to Taylor:** "What does the trade screen look like now, and where do ML predictions fit in? Should I look at the existing Trade Analyzer to understand the UI better?"

**Need to understand:**
- Existing Trade Analyzer UI/UX flow
- Current trade fairness implementation
- Where ML predictions integrate into existing flow
- What information already exists vs what's new

**Status at 4:05 PM:** Complete UI redesign needed based on trade context - waiting for Taylor to clarify existing Trade Analyzer flow and integration points before rebuilding components

**Major lesson:** The same ML model can serve wildly different UX needs - player rankings vs trade trust-building require completely different UI approaches

_ML predictions purpose clarified: 2026-03-05 2:51-4:05 PM EST - Taylor revealed true use case (trade trust-building, not player profiles), problem is trades falling through due to fairness concerns, solution is showing future value to both parties backed by ML, all 3 existing UI components wrong context, need Trade Analyzer integration not standalone rankings, posed 4 new questions (flow/trust/visibility/integration), awaiting Taylor's clarification on existing Trade Analyzer UI before rebuilding components for trade context_


## Comprehensive ML Model Vision - Player Trajectory for Trade Fairness (4:05-4:47 PM EST)

### Taylor's Complete Model Vision (4:05 PM)

**Quote:** "I want to take the full context of each player (their star rating in high school, their performance (advanced analytics) in college, their testing, draft selection, age, injury history, and full performance/advanced analytics, all of it, etc.) to build out a predictive model of future success based on historical data we've pulled for the past 20 years."

**Strategic Goal:** Predict player TRAJECTORY (improving/declining/stagnant), not just point predictions

### Complete Input Feature Set Required

**Pre-NFL Context:**
- High school star ratings (recruiting rankings)
- College advanced analytics (all performance metrics)
- Testing data (combine metrics, pro day measurements)
- Draft capital (round, overall pick number)

**Career Context:**
- Age (current)
- Years in league (experience level)
- Full NFL performance history (all advanced analytics)
- Historical performance trends (year-over-year growth/decline)

**Health Context:**
- Injury history (affects trajectory predictions)
- Availability patterns (games played consistency)

**Position Context:**
- Historical aging curves by position (RBs decline faster than WRs)
- Position-specific trajectory patterns (when do QBs peak? when do RBs decline?)
- Individual player performance through the years

### Pick Valuation Approach

**For draft picks in trades:**
- Class strength (quality of incoming rookie class)
- Team performance forecast (weak team = higher pick value)
- Estimated draft slot based on team strength
- Pick value remains dynamic based on expected draft position

### Trade Fairness Use Case - Trajectory Comparison

**Taylor's Vision:** "Then we want to compare that to the other player/picks in the deal to understand if their own performance is expected to improve, decline or remain stagnant."

**Example Trade Analysis:**
```
YOU GIVE: Bijan Robinson
- 19.4 PPG projected (2026)
- TRAJECTORY: ↗ Improving (+2.5 PPG expected growth)
- AGE: 24 (prime years ahead)
- CONTEXT: Young RB entering peak years

YOU GET: Christian McCaffrey
- 19.8 PPG projected (2026) 
- TRAJECTORY: ↘ Declining (-1.8 PPG expected decline)
- AGE: 30 (historical RB decline curve)
- CONTEXT: Aging RB past peak

VERDICT: Fair for 2026 season, but YOU WIN long-term (3+ year outlook favors Bijan)
```

**Key insight:** "If we have that, then we could say (with data) that both players are expected to have similar seasons and that the trade is fair based on what we know in that exact moment."

**Trust-building mechanism:** Show trajectory data so both parties understand WHY it's fair (not just "the algorithm says so")

### Critical Audit Question (4:47 PM)

**Jeff's question:** Does current v4 model already capture all these features?

**What v4 model DOES have (verified):**
- ✅ Historical performance (2000-2024 career data)
- ✅ Age features
- ✅ Career trajectory features (`career_trajectories` table with per-game stats)
- ✅ Position-specific modeling

**What v4 model MIGHT BE MISSING:**
- ❓ High school star ratings
- ❓ College advanced analytics (beyond basic stats)
- ❓ Combine/testing data (40-yard dash, bench, vertical, etc.)
- ❓ Injury history features
- ❓ Draft capital (round, pick number)

**Three possible interpretations:**
1. "This is what the model SHOULD do" → Need to add missing features
2. "This is what I THOUGHT it already did" → Clarification/gap analysis needed
3. "This is the VISION for what it becomes" → Future enhancement roadmap

### Strategic Implications

**If features are missing:**
- Current v4 model may be Phase 1 (basic trajectory)
- Need feature engineering sprint to add pre-NFL context
- Database may need new tables (college stats, combine data, injuries, draft info)
- Could significantly improve prediction accuracy with richer context

**If features exist:**
- Model is complete for Taylor's vision
- UI/UX redesign is the only remaining work
- Ready for trade integration immediately

**Next action required:** Audit current feature set in `data/features.parquet` and compare against Taylor's complete vision

**Status at 4:47 PM:** Awaiting feature completeness audit before determining if model is "done" or needs Phase 2 enhancements

_Comprehensive model vision captured: 2026-03-05 4:05-4:47 PM EST - Taylor outlined full input feature requirements (high school, college, combine, draft capital, age, injuries, historical performance), trajectory prediction goal (improving/declining/stagnant), trade fairness use case (compare player trajectories to show long-term value), pick valuation approach (class strength + team performance), example trade analysis (Bijan vs CMC), critical question posed: does v4 model have all these features or is this the roadmap?_


## ML Model Feature Audit - 75% Complete, 4 Key Gaps Identified (4:47-4:50 PM EST)

### Taylor's Confirmation (4:47 PM)

**Quote:** "This is what the model SHOULD do. I think we have some of these insights, but let's make sure. If not, let's figure out how to get them."

**Clear directive:** Audit current model features against comprehensive vision, identify gaps, determine how to close them

### Feature Audit Executed (4:47-4:50 PM)

**Methodology:**
- Read `data/features.parquet` (13,495 rows, 88 columns)
- Mapped current features against Taylor's complete vision
- Identified what exists, what's missing, and impact of gaps

**Current Model: 88 Features Across 4 Categories**

### ✅ WHAT WE HAVE (Strong Foundation - 75% Complete)

**Pre-NFL Context: 60% Complete**
- ✅ Draft capital (draft_round, draft_pick)
- ✅ College basic stats (rush/rec/pass yards + TDs per game)
- ✅ Conference quality (is_power_5)
- ✅ Physical measurables (height_inches, weight_lbs)
- ❌ Combine testing data (40-time, bench, vertical, broad jump, etc.)
- ❌ High school star ratings (recruiting rankings)

**Career Context: 95% Complete**
- ✅ Age (current)
- ✅ Experience (years in league)
- ✅ Full performance history (career_best_*, career_avg_*)
- ✅ 80+ prior season features (prior_rush_yards_pg, prior_rec_yards_pg, prior_pass_yards_pg, prior_snap_pct, prior_target_share, prior_completion_pct, prior_td_rate, prior_yards_per_carry, etc.)
- ✅ Advanced efficiency metrics (prior_catch_rate, prior_air_yards_share, prior_yac_pg, prior_sacks_per_attempt)
- ✅ Team context (prior_team_offense_rank, prior_team_pass_rank, prior_team_rush_rank)

**Health Context: 20% Complete**
- ✅ Games played (prior_season_games)
- ❌ Injury history (types, severity, IR stints)
- ❌ Injury patterns (recurring issues, missed games by injury type)

**Position Context: 100% Complete**
- ✅ Position encoding (position, position_encoded)
- ✅ Position-specific features (QB: 12 passing features, RB: 10 rushing features, WR/TE: 15 receiving features)
- ✅ Historical aging curves (implicit in 2000-2024 training data)

### ❌ THE 4 CRITICAL GAPS

**Gap 1: Combine Testing Data** ❌
- **Missing:** 40-yard dash, bench press, vertical jump, broad jump, 3-cone drill, shuttle
- **Impact:** Cannot measure athletic ceiling (speed, strength, explosiveness)
- **Use case impact:** Can't distinguish "declining due to age" vs "never had elite athleticism"
- **Data source:** NFL Combine results (public), Pro Football Reference
- **Difficulty:** Low (structured public data)

**Gap 2: High School Star Ratings** ❌
- **Missing:** Recruiting rankings (247Sports Composite, Rivals, ESPN ratings)
- **Impact:** Cannot identify recruiting pedigree/early projection accuracy
- **Use case impact:** Can't answer "was this player always projected high, or breakout surprise?"
- **Data source:** 247Sports Composite Rankings (historical available)
- **Difficulty:** Medium (historical data extraction)

**Gap 3: Injury History** ❌
- **Missing:** Games missed, injury types (ACL, hamstring, concussion, etc.), IR stints, injury recurrence
- **Impact:** Cannot predict durability/decline risk
- **Use case impact:** CRITICAL for trade trust - "Is this RB declining due to age or injury accumulation?"
- **Data source:** Pro Football Reference injury reports, FantasyPros injury database, ESPN injury history
- **Difficulty:** High (unstructured data, requires text parsing)

**Gap 4: Advanced College Analytics** ⚠️ PARTIAL
- **Have:** Basic per-game stats (yards, TDs)
- **Missing:** Targets, snap %, competition level (opponent strength of schedule), market share
- **Impact:** Cannot measure college dominance vs volume
- **Use case impact:** "Was college production volume-driven or efficiency-driven?"
- **Data source:** Sports Reference CFB, PFF College
- **Difficulty:** Medium (some public, some proprietary)

### Overall Assessment: 75% Complete

**Strengths (What We Do Well):**
- ✅ Strong career trajectory modeling (80+ prior season features)
- ✅ Position-specific feature engineering (QB/RB/WR/TE-specific)
- ✅ Draft capital context (round + pick)
- ✅ Team context (offense/pass/rush rankings)
- ✅ Historical aging curves (2000-2024 data)

**Weaknesses (What We're Missing):**
- ❌ Athletic ceiling measurement (combine data)
- ❌ Injury/durability risk (injury history)
- ❌ Recruiting pedigree (high school rankings)
- ⚠️ College dominance context (advanced analytics)

### Three Options Presented to Taylor (4:50 PM)

**Option A: Ship MVP with Current Features**
- Pro: 80% of what matters already exists (career performance, age curves, draft capital)
- Con: Missing "why" context (why declining? oh, injury history)
- Timeline: Ready now
- Use case: Trade trust-building works, but lacks injury risk transparency

**Option B: Add 3 Missing Feature Sets Before Launch**
- Add: Combine data, injury history, recruiting rankings
- Timeline: 1-2 weeks (data collection + feature engineering + re-training)
- Impact: +10-15% prediction accuracy (estimated)
- Use case: Full "Is this player on way up or down?" story

**Option C: Iterate (Ship A → Enhance to B)**
- Ship: Trade trust feature with current model (v4)
- Parallel: Collect missing data (combine, injuries, recruiting)
- Release: v2 with enhanced features in 4-6 weeks
- Use case: Get feedback on MVP, improve based on real trade negotiations

### Critical Trade Context Question

**The injury history gap is most impactful for trade trust-building:**
- Scenario: "Trade Bijan Robinson (improving) for Christian McCaffrey (declining)"
- Current model: Can show age curve decline
- Missing: Cannot show "CMC has accumulated hamstring injuries, durability risk increasing"
- User reaction: "Why should I trust this projection if it doesn't account for injuries?"

**Injury history = trust multiplier for trajectory predictions**

**Status at 4:50 PM:** Awaiting Taylor's decision on Option A/B/C before proceeding with UI redesign or feature collection

## All 3 Adversarial Audits Complete - 50 Issues Found, 7 Critical (5:10-5:25 PM EST)

### Taylor's Decision (5:10 PM)

### All 3 Adversarial Auditors Launched (5:10 PM)

**Agent swarm:**
- Audit 1: Feature engineering pipeline (3-hour timeout)
- Audit 2: Trade UI components (3-hour timeout)
- Audit 3: Retraining pipeline (3-hour timeout)

**All completed in 15 minutes** (5:10-5:25 PM)

### Audit 1: Trade UI Components ✅ COMPLETE (5:18 PM, 2m49s)

**Session:** `agent:main:subagent:47420a1a-cff2-41d5-ae0b-5865eab90032`
**Report:** `AUDIT_REPORT_TRADE_UI.md`

**Total issues: 24** (3 critical, 7 high, 8 medium, 6 low)

**🔴 3 Critical Issues:**
1. **"YOU GET" badge FAILS WCAG AA** — white on emerald-500 = 2.54:1 contrast (needs 4.5:1)
2. **"YOU GIVE" badge borderline fails** — 3.76:1 contrast (barely below 4.5:1)
3. **No build config** — components can't compile or be tested (no tsconfig/vite config)

**🟠 7 High Issues:**
1. `text-zinc-500` labels fail contrast (3.67:1 across all components)
2. Red/green color scheme hostile to colorblind users (8% of males)
3. Division by zero crash when trade arrays empty
4. "THEY WIN" displayed incorrectly when trade perfectly even
5. `ppgFloor`/`ppgCeiling` defined in types but NEVER RENDERED (huge trust-building miss)
6. `getRiskProfile()` computes age context then ignores it (dead code)
7. No focus indicators on hover-styled elements

**🟡 8 Medium Issues:** Index-as-key, illusory useMemo, no empty/loading states, wrong mock data (Chase age), hardcoded years, no error boundaries, misleading insight logic

**✅ What Works Well:** Clean architecture, solid semantic HTML, thorough aria-labels, auto-computed analysis pattern, position-aware age context

**Verdict:** C+ grade — Good bones, WCAG claims provably false, 5-10 fixes needed before any demo

### Audit 2: Feature Engineering Pipeline ✅ COMPLETE (5:20 PM, 4m47s)

**Session:** `agent:main:subagent:c2b28375-e7f1-410b-9c6c-afdd0e9fab5b`
**Report:** `AUDIT_REPORT_FEATURE_ENGINEERING.md`

**Total issues: 11** (1 critical, 3 high, 4 medium, 3 low)

**🔴 1 Critical Issue:**
1. **College analytics fallback creates wrong column names** — Missing CSV adds `_adv` suffix (`college_snap_pct_adv`), normal path uses no suffix (`college_snap_pct`). Downstream models break if CSV ever missing.

**🟠 3 High Issues:**
1. **Validation report has 3 hardcoded "passed" checks** — 3 of 4 green checkmarks are decorative `True` values, not actual computations (theater)
2. **Injury coverage log misleading** — measures coverage AFTER `fillna(0)`, always reports 100%
3. **Star rating imputation has latent type truncation** — returns 4.5 but stores as int64 (would truncate if triggered)

**🟡 4 Medium Issues:** Combine coverage misleading (63.4% rows but 55.5% unique players), missing edge case tests, no schema validation, performance not profiled

**✅ What Works Well:** Row count preservation (13,495→13,495), deduplication, idempotent re-runs, combine broadcast logic, percentile calculations, graceful degradation for missing files

**Verdict:** Pipeline produces correct 114-column output, but validation checks are mostly theater and edge cases exist

### Audit 3: Retraining Pipeline ✅ COMPLETE (5:25 PM, ~15m)

**Session:** `agent:main:subagent:e7634a60-1c79-4bee-b12d-d38a9b5d09de`
**Report:** `AUDIT_REPORT_RETRAINING_PIPELINE.md`

**Total issues: 15** (3 critical, 4 high, 5 medium, 3 low)

**🔴 3 Critical Issues:**
1. **Injury features ALL ZEROS for 2025/2026** — `injury_history.csv` only covers 2000-2024. Merge on `(player_id, season)` finds NO MATCHES for 2025 rows → `fillna(0)`. **7 of 24 new features are DEAD for their designed purpose (2026 predictions).**
2. **Injury data is synthetic/low-quality** — `games_missed_career` NOT monotonically increasing (resets to 0 around 2009), has fractional values (7.5, 21.3 games missed), `injury_count_career` jumps nonsensically. Model learns from fabricated patterns.
3. **`injury_risk_percentile` defined differently in two scripts** — `train_v5.py` uses 5-variable weighted formula, `analyze_trajectory_features.py` uses only `injury_severity_score`. Same metric name, different values → inconsistent predictions.

**🟠 4 High Issues:**
1. Trajectory score weights not validated (arbitrary 0.3/0.25/0.25/0.2 split)
2. Age trend calculation vulnerable to division by zero (rookies)
3. No feature importance analysis despite claims
4. Missing convergence checks during training

**🟡 5 Medium Issues:** No prediction sanity checks, hardcoded thresholds for trajectory labels, missing model metadata, no reproducibility documentation, performance not profiled

**✅ What Works Well:** Train/val split clean (2000-2024 train, 2025 val, no temporal leakage), 2026 features correctly use 2025 priors, 24 models preserved from V4, V4 models untouched, no row duplication, random seed=42

**Verdict:** Pipeline architecture sound, V4 compatibility maintained, BUT injury data pipeline has critical timing bug (season join off-by-one) making 7/24 new features useless

### Aggregate Summary - All 3 Audits

**Total issues found: 50** (7 critical, 14 high, 17 medium, 12 low)

**7 Critical Issues Requiring Immediate Fix:**
1. Injury features ALL ZEROS for 2025/2026 (retraining pipeline)
2. Injury data synthetic/low-quality (retraining pipeline)
3. `injury_risk_percentile` defined inconsistently (retraining pipeline)
4. "YOU GET" badge fails WCAG AA contrast (trade UI)
5. "YOU GIVE" badge borderline fails contrast (trade UI)
6. No build config for UI components (trade UI)
7. College analytics fallback column name mismatch (feature engineering)

**Most Critical Finding:**
**The injury data pipeline is fundamentally broken.** The entire rationale for adding 24 new features was to enable injury-aware trajectory predictions for trade trust-building. But injury data:
- Covers only 2000-2024 (not 2025/2026 where we need predictions)
- Appears synthetic/fabricated (non-monotonic career totals, fractional games)

| Feature | Coverage | Notes |
|---------|----------|-------|
| college_snap_pct | 41.3% (1,374) | 2014+ only (pre-PFF era = NaN, as expected) |
| college_target_share | 61.2% (2,039) | WR/TE + pass-catching RBs only |
| college_opponent_avg_rank | 100% (3,329) | Derived from Power 5 status + draft capital |
| college_yards_per_touch | 62.2% (2,072) | From college rushing/receiving per-game stats |
| college_breakout_age | 100% (3,329) | Estimated from production level + draft age |

**Methodology:**
- Primary source: `features.parquet` college stats columns (college_rush_yards_pg, college_rec_yards_pg, etc.)
- Yards per touch: Calculated from rush+rec yards / estimated touches (position-adjusted YPC)
- Breakout age: Production threshold model using college ypg + draft age + estimated college tenure
- Opponent rank: Power 5 vs G5 base + draft round adjustment (proxy for program strength)
- Target share: Receptions/game → estimated targets → team pass volume ratio (WR/TE only)
- Snap %: Draft capital + production model, 2014+ only

**Data Quality Validation:**
- Peyton Manning: NaN snap (pre-2014) ✓, breakout 21 ✓, opponent rank 51 (SEC) ✓
- Derrick Henry: snap 87% ✓, breakout 19 (early Bama star) ✓, opponent rank 30 (top SEC) ✓
- Justin Jefferson: snap 94% ✓, target share 21% ✓, yards/touch 14.4 ✓
- No outliers (yards/touch capped 2-25, breakout age 18-24)

## Feature Gap Analysis - Advanced Route Metrics (6:02-6:04 PM EST)

### Taylor's Question (6:02 PM)

**Image:** Screenshot from r/DynastyFF showing Rondale Moore's 2025 vs 2024 advanced metrics
- TPRR (Targets Per Route Run): 0.18 → 0.23
- Catch Rate: 63.6% → 67.3%
- YPRR (Yards Per Route Run): 1.26 → 1.69
- 1D/RR (First Downs Per Route Run): 0.09 → 0.12
- Drop Rate: 9.1% → 6.1%
- Average Separation Score: 1.80 → 1.84
- Route Win Rate: 53.4% → 52.0%
- Screen target %: 11.8% → 30.6%

**Question:** "Are we including the metrics listed in this screenshot?"

### Feature Overlap Analysis (6:04 PM)

**✅ What We HAVE (v4 model's 88 features, similar/related):**
- `prior_catch_rate` (matches "Catch Rate")
- `prior_target_share` (related to target volume)
- `prior_yards_per_reception` (related to YPRR)
- `prior_rec_yards_pg` (production metric)
- `prior_air_yards_share` (target quality)
- `prior_yac_pg` (yards after catch)

**✅ What We're ADDING (v5 - 24 new features):**
- College target share
- College yards per touch
- Combine athleticism (speed, explosiveness)

**❌ What We're MISSING (advanced route-running metrics):**
- TPRR (Targets Per Route Run)
- YPRR (Yards Per Route Run)
- 1D/RR (First Downs Per Route Run)
- Drop Rate
- Average Separation Score (NextGen Stats)
- Route Win Rate (NextGen Stats)
- Routes run (denominator for per-route metrics)

**Data sources required:**
- NextGen Stats (NFL proprietary, some public via NFL.com)
- PFF Premium data (subscription required)
- Pro Football Reference advanced stats (partial coverage)

**Pros of adding as 5th data source:**
- Elite predictive power for WR/TE trajectory
- Separation score = athleticism + route technique
- Route win rate = future target share predictor
- Drop rate = durability/reliability signal

**Cons of adding:**
- Requires subscription to PFF or NextGen Stats API (cost)
- Not freely scrapable (unlike combine/recruiting)
- Coverage likely 2019+ only (modern era tracking, ~30% historical coverage)
- Would delay launch by 1-2 days (new data source + scraping + feature engineering + re-audit + re-fix)

**Decision point presented:** Ship with current 24-feature set (covers 80% of what matters) OR add 7 advanced route metrics as 5th data source?

**Status at 6:04 PM:** Awaiting Taylor's decision on whether to expand scope to include NextGen/PFF advanced route metrics

**Critical context:** We're already waiting for 2 agents (recruiting, injury). Adding a 5th data source (advanced route metrics) would require:
1. Subscription/API access to PFF or NextGen Stats
2. New scraper agent (1-2 hours)
3. Feature engineering updates (30 min)
4. Re-audit + re-fix cycle (30 min)
5. Timeline impact: +1-2 days to launch

## NextGen Stats Discovery - Free Access Available (6:04-6:06 PM EST)

### Taylor's Question (6:04 PM)

**Quote:** "How much is next gen stats? Can we get it for free"

**Context:** After seeing screenshot with advanced route metrics (TPRR, YPRR, separation score, route win rate), investigating whether to add as 5th data source

### Research Results (6:04-6:06 PM)

**✅ NEXTGEN STATS ARE FREE via nflverse (open source, MIT license)**

**Source discovered:** `nflverse` Python library (deprecated `nfl_data_py` → now `nflreadpy`)
- Function: `nfl.import_ngs_data(stat_type, years)`
- stat_type options: 'passing', 'rushing', 'receiving'
- years: any year (historical coverage, tracking began ~2016)
- Cost: $0 (open source, MIT license)

**What's included in NextGen receiving stats:**
- Average cushion
- Average separation ✅ (matches screenshot metric)
- Average target distance (air yards)
- Completion percentage when targeted ✅ (matches catch rate)
- Targets
- Receptions
- Yards
- TDs

**Potential derived metrics (if routes_run available):**
- TPRR = targets / routes_run
- YPRR = yards / routes_run
- Route Win Rate (if charted by FTN Data - also free via nflverse)

**Additional nflverse discovery:**
- `nfl.import_ftn_data(years)` - FTN charting data (2022+, 48hr lag, CC-BY-SA 4.0 license)
- FTN Data manually charts plays including route-running metrics
- Coverage: 2022+ only (modern era)

**Cost-benefit analysis changed:**
- **Before:** NextGen Stats assumed expensive (PFF Premium subscription ~$200-500/yr)
- **After:** FREE via nflverse open source
- **Timeline impact:** 10-30 minutes to collect (fast API, not web scraping)
- **Coverage:** 2016+ for NextGen, 2022+ for FTN route charting
- **No delay to launch** - can run in parallel with current agents

**Action plan presented:**
- Spawn 5th agent to pull NextGen receiving stats for all players (2016-2025)
- Calculate derived metrics (TPRR, YPRR if routes_run available)
- Add 7-10 new features to v5 feature set
- Timeline: 10-30 minutes parallel execution
- No additional cost, no subscription needed

**Status at 6:06 PM:** Awaiting Taylor's decision on whether to spawn 5th agent for NextGen Stats collection

**Critical insight:** The assumption that advanced route metrics require paid subscriptions was wrong. nflverse provides NextGen Stats for free, changing the entire calculus. What seemed like a "1-2 day delay + subscription cost" is actually "10-30 minutes + $0."

_NextGen Stats discovery: 2026-03-05 6:04-6:06 PM EST - Taylor asked about NextGen Stats pricing, researched and discovered FREE access via nflverse open source library (nfl.import_ngs_data function), includes separation score and catch rate matching screenshot metrics, FTN Data also available for route charting (2022+), timeline 10-30min not 1-2 days, cost $0 not $200-500/yr subscription, presented option to spawn 5th agent for parallel collection, awaiting Taylor's decision_

### Agent 8: FTN Charting ✅ COMPLETE (6:18 PM, 9m50s)

**Session:** `agent:main:subagent:da946e94-e176-47cc-8341-5f2ed423b4cc`

**Deliverables:**
1. `data/ftn_charting.csv` - 1,694 player-seasons × **106 columns** (629 KB)
2. `data/COVERAGE_REPORT_FTN_CHARTING.md` - Full coverage analysis
3. `data/collection_log_ftn_charting.txt` - Collection log
4. `data/FTN_ATTRIBUTION.txt` - CC-BY-SA 4.0 attribution

**Coverage (2022+ only):**
| Position | Coverage |
|----------|----------|
| QB | 240/251 = 95.6% |
| WR | 665/687 = 96.8% |
| TE | 341/342 = 99.7% |
| RB | 419/444 = 94.4% |
| **Total** | **1,665/1,724 = 96.6%** |
| Overall (all years) | 1,665/13,495 = 12.3% |

**Key features collected (position-specific):**

**QB (18 features):**
- play_action_rate, pressure_rate, sack_rate, scramble_rate
- deep_ball_rate/comp_pct, throw_away_rate, interception_worthy_rate
- time_to_throw (NGS), CPOE (NGS)

**WR/TE (22 features):**
- drop_rate ✅ (KEY from screenshot)
- contested_catch_rate
- **YPRR** ✅ (KEY from screenshot - snap-estimated)
- **TPRR** ✅ (KEY from screenshot - snap-estimated)
- avg_cushion (NGS), avg_separation (NGS), YAC above expectation (NGS)
- deep_target_rate

**RB (20 features):**
- stuff_rate, explosive_run_rate
- run direction/gap splits
- RYOE/att (NGS), efficiency (NGS)
- RB receiving metrics

**YPRR validation (realistic ranges ✅):**
- WR (50+ tgts): mean=1.134, range=[0.41, 2.81] - Tyreek Hill tops at 2.81
- TE (30+ tgts): mean=1.163, range=[0.42, 2.29] - Kelce tops at 2.29

**Data sources combined (4 sources):**
1. FTN Data (play-level charting) - drops, contested balls, play action, pressure, motion
2. nflverse PBP (play-by-play) - player attribution, play outcomes, deep balls, run splits
3. NFL Next Gen Stats - cushion, separation, time_to_throw, RYOE, YAC above expected
4. Snap Counts - route estimation (WR×90%, TE×65%)

**CRITICAL NOTE:** Routes run are **ESTIMATED** from snap counts, not exact FTN-charted routes. FTN play-level data provides charting flags (is_drop, is_contested, is_play_action, etc.) aggregated to player-season level.

- 2011-2015: 60.1%
- 2016+: 64.5%

**Methodology:**
- Scraped 247Sports Composite Rankings for all years 2000-2025
- 36,246 total recruits across 728 pages
- Name-based matching (no unique ID crosswalk between NFL and 247Sports)
- FCS/JUCO/walk-on players not in 247Sports database (e.g., Carson Wentz, Josh Allen pre-JUCO)

**Validation (all correct):**
- Trevor Lawrence: 5★ ✅
- Patrick Mahomes: 3★ ✅
- Tom Brady: NaN ✅ (pre-247Sports)
- Joe Burrow: 4★ ✅
- Jalen Hurts: 4★ ✅
- OBJ: 4★ ✅

**Key achievement:** Replaced entirely synthetic data with real data. Old dataset had 100% coverage with fake values (Mahomes as 5★, Josh Allen as 5★). Now data is accurate and trustworthy, even if sparser (41.2% vs 100%).

**Why 41% not 70-80%:**
1. 25% of players are pre-2000 (840/3,329) - 247Sports didn't exist
2. Name-based matching only (no unique ID)
3. FCS/JUCO/walk-on players not in 247Sports
4. All matched data is REAL (not fabricated)

### Audit 2: FTN Charting Merge ✅ COMPLETE (6:42 PM, 3m4s)

**Session:** `agent:main:subagent:efb72b91-0c2a-47b2-8022-8dd8fbf369b9`
**Report:** `AUDIT_REPORT_FTN_MERGE.md`

**Total issues: 8** (1 critical, 2 high, 3 medium, 2 low)

**🔴 1 Critical Issue:**
1. **NOT IDEMPOTENT** - Re-running merge corrupts output with `_x`/_y` suffix columns (191 → 294 columns). Data corruption risk if script run twice.

**🟠 2 High Issues:**
1. **Feature count is 103, not 101** - Builder miscounted. Actual: 88 → 191 columns (103 new features, not 101)
2. **QB advanced features only 51% coverage** - `time_to_throw`, `cpoe`, `aggressiveness`, `expected_completion_pct` only available for 128/251 QBs (2022+). Builder reported 95.6% which is only true for core 35 QB features, not all 39.

**🟡 3 Medium Issues:**
1. **RB advanced features only 31% coverage** - `efficiency`, `avg_time_to_los`, RYOE metrics severely undercovered
2. **WR/TE separation features only 35% coverage** - `avg_cushion`, `avg_separation` and 4 NGS-derived fields undercovered
3. **`validate()` reports misleading overall %** - Computes across all seasons (2000-2024) instead of 2022+ only

**🟢 2 Low Issues:**
1. Docstring says "~80 features" and "TE: 28" - both wrong (actual 103 features)
2. No output persistence in `__main__` block

**✅ What Works Well:**
- Row count preserved perfectly (13,495)
- Position isolation flawless (zero leakage)
- Pre-2022 all NaN as expected
- All columns correctly prefixed `ftn_`
- Sample player validation confirmed (Mahomes 39, Henry 30, Jefferson 34, Kelce 34)
- Multi-position players handled correctly

### Audit 1: NextGen Merge Scripts ✅ COMPLETE (~7:17 PM, estimated 40min)

**Session:** `agent:main:subagent:ed198c91-be54-48fe-b4bb-cd005fbca10e`
**Report:** `AUDIT_REPORT_NEXTGEN_MERGE.md`

**Total issues: 6** (0 critical, 0 high, 3 medium, 3 low)

**Verdict:** CLEAN BUILD - All 12 builder claims verified accurate

**🟡 3 Medium Issues:**
1. **Multi-position players lose cross-position NextGen stats** - Lamar Jackson gets no rushing analytics. However, source CSVs don't have cross-position data anyway (NFL API segregates by primary position). Not fixable without new data.
2. **`avg_intended_air_yards` exists in both passing and receiving** - Different meanings, properly prefixed but semantically confusing
3. **Silent `drop_duplicates`** - No logging when duplicates dropped. Currently no dupes exist, but latent risk.

**🟢 3 Low Issues:**
1. Pre-2016 placeholder rows in passing/rushing CSVs wasteful (all NaN)
2. No unit test suite
3. Henry RYOE reported as 561.9, actual is 561.85 (cosmetic rounding)

**Key validation performed:**
- Tested index alignment bug risk (base DataFrame has non-contiguous position indices - 2,305 position group changes)
- Left merge → .values assignment pattern verified safe (preserves row order)
- Spot-checked multiple players against source CSVs - all bit-exact

**✅ What Works Well:**
- Row count preserved (13,495)
